﻿MANIFESTO OF THE COMMUNIST PARTY | communistmanifesto
[From the English edition of 1888, edited by Friedrich Engels] | communistmanifesto
A spectre is haunting Europe--the spectre of Communism. | communistmanifesto
All the Powers of old Europe have entered into a holy alliance to | communistmanifesto
exorcise this spectre: Pope and Czar, Metternich and Guizot, | communistmanifesto
French Radicals and German police-spies. | communistmanifesto
Where is the party in opposition that has not been decried as | communistmanifesto
Communistic by its opponents in power?  Where is the Opposition | communistmanifesto
that has not hurled back the branding reproach of Communism, | communistmanifesto
against the more advanced opposition parties, as well as against | communistmanifesto
its reactionary adversaries? | communistmanifesto
Two things result from this fact. | communistmanifesto
I.  Communism is already acknowledged by all European Powers | communistmanifesto
to be itself a Power. | communistmanifesto
II.  It is high time that Communists should openly, in the | communistmanifesto
face of the whole world, publish their views, their aims, their | communistmanifesto
tendencies, and meet this nursery tale of the Spectre of | communistmanifesto
Communism with a Manifesto of the party itself. | communistmanifesto
To this end, Communists of various nationalities have | communistmanifesto
assembled in London, and sketched the following Manifesto, to be | communistmanifesto
published in the English, French, German, Italian, Flemish and | communistmanifesto
Danish languages. | communistmanifesto
I.  BOURGEOIS AND PROLETARIANS | communistmanifesto
The history of all hitherto existing societies is the history | communistmanifesto
of class struggles. | communistmanifesto
Freeman and slave, patrician and plebeian, lord and serf, | communistmanifesto
guild-master and journeyman, in a word, oppressor and oppressed, | communistmanifesto
stood in constant opposition to one another, carried on an | communistmanifesto
uninterrupted, now hidden, now open fight, a fight that each time | communistmanifesto
ended, either in a revolutionary re-constitution of society at | communistmanifesto
large, or in the common ruin of the contending classes. | communistmanifesto
In the earlier epochs of history, we find almost everywhere a | communistmanifesto
complicated arrangement of society into various orders, a | communistmanifesto
manifold gradation of social rank.  In ancient Rome we have | communistmanifesto
patricians, knights, plebeians, slaves; in the Middle Ages, | communistmanifesto
feudal lords, vassals, guild-masters, journeymen, apprentices, | communistmanifesto
serfs; in almost all of these classes, again, subordinate | communistmanifesto
gradations. | communistmanifesto
The modern bourgeois society that has sprouted from the ruins | communistmanifesto
of feudal society has not done away with class antagonisms.  It | communistmanifesto
has but established new classes, new conditions of oppression, | communistmanifesto
new forms of struggle in place of the old ones.  Our epoch, the | communistmanifesto
epoch of the bourgeoisie, possesses, however, this distinctive | communistmanifesto
feature: it has simplified the class antagonisms. Society as a | communistmanifesto
whole is more and more splitting up into two great hostile camps, | communistmanifesto
into two great classes, directly facing each other: Bourgeoisie | communistmanifesto
and Proletariat. | communistmanifesto
From the serfs of the Middle Ages sprang the chartered burghers | communistmanifesto
of the earliest towns.  From these burgesses the first elements | communistmanifesto
of the bourgeoisie were developed. | communistmanifesto
The discovery of America, the rounding of the Cape, opened up | communistmanifesto
fresh ground for the rising bourgeoisie. The East-Indian and | communistmanifesto
Chinese markets, the colonisation of America, trade with | communistmanifesto
the colonies, the increase in the means of exchange and in | communistmanifesto
commodities generally, gave to commerce, to navigation, to | communistmanifesto
industry, an impulse never before known, and thereby, to the | communistmanifesto
revolutionary element in the tottering feudal society, a rapid | communistmanifesto
development. | communistmanifesto
The feudal system of industry, under which industrial production | communistmanifesto
was monopolised by closed guilds, now no longer sufficed for the | communistmanifesto
growing wants of the new markets.  The manufacturing system took | communistmanifesto
its place.  The guild-masters were pushed on one side by the | communistmanifesto
manufacturing middle class; division of labour between the | communistmanifesto
different corporate guilds vanished in the face of division of | communistmanifesto
labour in each single workshop. | communistmanifesto
Meantime the markets kept ever growing, the demand ever rising. | communistmanifesto
Even manufacture no longer sufficed.  Thereupon, steam and | communistmanifesto
machinery revolutionised industrial production.  The place of | communistmanifesto
manufacture was taken by the giant, Modern Industry, the place of | communistmanifesto
the industrial middle class, by industrial millionaires, the | communistmanifesto
leaders of whole industrial armies, the modern bourgeois. | communistmanifesto
Modern industry has established the world-market, for which the | communistmanifesto
discovery of America paved the way.  This market has given an | communistmanifesto
immense development to commerce, to navigation, to communication | communistmanifesto
by land.  This development has, in its time, reacted on the | communistmanifesto
extension of industry; and in proportion as industry, commerce, | communistmanifesto
navigation, railways extended, in the same proportion the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie developed, increased its capital, and pushed into the | communistmanifesto
background  every class handed down from the Middle Ages. | communistmanifesto
We see, therefore, how the modern bourgeoisie is itself the | communistmanifesto
product of a long course of development, of a series of | communistmanifesto
revolutions in the modes of production and of exchange. | communistmanifesto
Each step in the development of the bourgeoisie was accompanied | communistmanifesto
by a corresponding political advance of that class.  An | communistmanifesto
oppressed class under the sway of the feudal nobility, an | communistmanifesto
armed and self-governing association in the mediaeval commune; | communistmanifesto
here independent urban republic (as in Italy and Germany), | communistmanifesto
there taxable "third estate" of the monarchy (as in France), | communistmanifesto
afterwards, in the  period of manufacture proper, serving either | communistmanifesto
the semi-feudal or the absolute monarchy as a counterpoise | communistmanifesto
against the nobility, and, in fact, corner-stone of the great | communistmanifesto
monarchies in general, the bourgeoisie has at last, since the | communistmanifesto
establishment of Modern Industry and of the world-market, | communistmanifesto
conquered for itself, in the modern representative State, | communistmanifesto
exclusive political sway.  The executive of the modern State is | communistmanifesto
but a committee for managing the common affairs of the whole | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie, historically, has played a most revolutionary | communistmanifesto
part. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie, wherever it has got the upper hand, has put an | communistmanifesto
end to all feudal, patriarchal, idyllic relations.  It has | communistmanifesto
pitilessly torn asunder the motley feudal ties that bound man to | communistmanifesto
his "natural superiors," and has left remaining no other nexus | communistmanifesto
between man and man than naked self-interest, than callous "cash | communistmanifesto
payment."  It has drowned the most heavenly ecstasies of | communistmanifesto
religious fervour, of chivalrous enthusiasm, of philistine | communistmanifesto
sentimentalism, in the icy water of egotistical calculation.  It | communistmanifesto
has resolved personal worth into exchange value, and in place of | communistmanifesto
the numberless and indefeasible chartered freedoms, has set up that | communistmanifesto
single, unconscionable freedom--Free Trade.  In one word, for | communistmanifesto
exploitation, veiled by religious and political illusions, naked, | communistmanifesto
shameless, direct, brutal exploitation. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie has stripped of its halo every occupation | communistmanifesto
hitherto honoured and looked up to with reverent awe.  It has | communistmanifesto
converted the physician, the lawyer, the priest, the poet, the | communistmanifesto
man of science, into its paid wage labourers. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie has torn away from the family its sentimental | communistmanifesto
veil, and has reduced the family relation to a mere money | communistmanifesto
relation. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie has disclosed how it came to pass that the | communistmanifesto
brutal display of vigour in the Middle Ages, which Reactionists | communistmanifesto
so much admire, found its fitting complement in the most slothful | communistmanifesto
indolence.  It has been the first to show what man's activity can | communistmanifesto
bring about.  It has accomplished wonders far surpassing Egyptian | communistmanifesto
pyramids, Roman aqueducts, and Gothic cathedrals; it has | communistmanifesto
conducted expeditions that put in the shade all former Exoduses | communistmanifesto
of nations and crusades. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie cannot exist without constantly revolutionising | communistmanifesto
the instruments of production, and thereby the relations of | communistmanifesto
production, and with them the whole relations of society. | communistmanifesto
Conservation of the old modes of production in unaltered form, | communistmanifesto
was, on the contrary, the first condition of existence for all | communistmanifesto
earlier industrial classes. Constant revolutionising of | communistmanifesto
production, uninterrupted disturbance of all social conditions, | communistmanifesto
everlasting uncertainty and agitation distinguish the bourgeois | communistmanifesto
epoch from all earlier ones. All fixed, fast-frozen relations, | communistmanifesto
with their train of ancient and venerable prejudices and | communistmanifesto
opinions, are swept away, all new-formed ones become antiquated | communistmanifesto
before they can ossify. All that is solid melts into air, all | communistmanifesto
that is holy is profaned, and man is at last compelled to face | communistmanifesto
with sober senses, his real conditions of life, and his | communistmanifesto
relations with his kind. | communistmanifesto
The need of a constantly expanding market for its products | communistmanifesto
chases the bourgeoisie over the whole surface of the globe. It | communistmanifesto
must nestle everywhere, settle everywhere, establish connexions | communistmanifesto
everywhere. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie has through its exploitation of the world-market | communistmanifesto
given a cosmopolitan character to production and consumption in | communistmanifesto
every country.  To the great chagrin of Reactionists, it has | communistmanifesto
drawn from under the feet of industry the national ground on | communistmanifesto
which it stood.  All old-established national industries have | communistmanifesto
been destroyed or are daily being destroyed.  They are dislodged | communistmanifesto
by new industries, whose introduction becomes a life and death | communistmanifesto
question for all civilised nations, by industries that no longer | communistmanifesto
work up indigenous raw material, but raw material drawn from the | communistmanifesto
remotest zones; industries whose products are consumed, not only | communistmanifesto
at home, but in every quarter of the globe.  In place of the old | communistmanifesto
wants, satisfied by the productions of the country, we find new | communistmanifesto
wants, requiring for their satisfaction the products of distant | communistmanifesto
lands and climes.  In place of the old local and national | communistmanifesto
seclusion and self-sufficiency, we have intercourse in every | communistmanifesto
direction, universal inter-dependence of nations.  And as in | communistmanifesto
material, so also in intellectual production.  The intellectual | communistmanifesto
creations of individual nations become common property.  National | communistmanifesto
one-sidedness and narrow-mindedness become more and more | communistmanifesto
impossible, and from the numerous national and local literatures, | communistmanifesto
there arises a world literature. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie, by the rapid improvement of all instruments of | communistmanifesto
production, by the immensely facilitated means of communication, | communistmanifesto
draws all, even the most barbarian, nations into civilisation. | communistmanifesto
The cheap prices of its commodities are the heavy artillery with | communistmanifesto
which it batters down all Chinese walls, with which it forces the | communistmanifesto
barbarians' intensely obstinate hatred of foreigners to | communistmanifesto
capitulate.  It compels all nations, on pain of extinction, to | communistmanifesto
adopt the bourgeois mode of production; it compels them to | communistmanifesto
introduce what it calls civilisation into their midst, i.e., to | communistmanifesto
become bourgeois themselves.  In one word, it creates a world | communistmanifesto
after its own image. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie has subjected the country to the rule of the | communistmanifesto
towns.  It has created enormous cities, has greatly increased the | communistmanifesto
urban population as compared with the rural, and has thus rescued | communistmanifesto
a considerable part of the population from the idiocy of rural | communistmanifesto
life.  Just as it has made the country dependent on the towns, so | communistmanifesto
it has made barbarian and semi-barbarian countries dependent on | communistmanifesto
the civilised ones, nations of peasants on nations of bourgeois, | communistmanifesto
the East on the West. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeoisie keeps more and more doing away with the | communistmanifesto
scattered state of the population, of the means of production, | communistmanifesto
and of property.  It has agglomerated production, and has | communistmanifesto
concentrated property in a few hands.  The necessary consequence | communistmanifesto
of this was political centralisation.  Independent, or but | communistmanifesto
loosely connected provinces, with separate interests, laws, | communistmanifesto
governments and systems of taxation, became lumped together into | communistmanifesto
one nation, with one government, one code of laws, one national | communistmanifesto
class-interest, one frontier and one customs-tariff.  The | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie, during its rule of scarce one hundred years, has | communistmanifesto
created more massive and more colossal productive forces than | communistmanifesto
have all preceding generations together.  Subjection of Nature's | communistmanifesto
forces to man, machinery, application of chemistry to industry | communistmanifesto
and agriculture, steam-navigation, railways, electric telegraphs, | communistmanifesto
clearing of whole continents for cultivation, canalisation of | communistmanifesto
rivers, whole populations conjured out of the ground--what | communistmanifesto
earlier century had even a presentiment that such productive | communistmanifesto
forces slumbered in the lap of social labour? | communistmanifesto
We see then: the means of production and of exchange, on whose | communistmanifesto
foundation the bourgeoisie built itself up, were generated in | communistmanifesto
feudal society.  At a certain stage in the development of these | communistmanifesto
means of production and of exchange, the conditions under which | communistmanifesto
feudal society produced and exchanged, the feudal organisation of | communistmanifesto
agriculture and manufacturing industry, in one word, the feudal | communistmanifesto
relations of property became no longer compatible with the | communistmanifesto
already developed productive forces; they became so many fetters. | communistmanifesto
They had to be burst asunder; they were burst asunder. | communistmanifesto
Into their place stepped free competition, accompanied by a | communistmanifesto
social and political constitution adapted to it, and by the | communistmanifesto
economical and political sway of the bourgeois class. | communistmanifesto
A similar movement is going on before our own eyes.  Modern | communistmanifesto
bourgeois society with its relations of production, of exchange | communistmanifesto
and of property, a society that has conjured up such gigantic | communistmanifesto
means of production and of exchange, is like the sorcerer, who is | communistmanifesto
no longer able to control the powers of the nether world whom he | communistmanifesto
has called up by his spells.  For many a decade past the history | communistmanifesto
of industry and commerce is but the history of the revolt of | communistmanifesto
modern productive forces against modern conditions of production, | communistmanifesto
against the property relations that are the conditions for the | communistmanifesto
existence of the bourgeoisie and of its rule.  It is enough to | communistmanifesto
mention the commercial crises that by their periodical return put | communistmanifesto
on its trial, each time more threateningly, the existence of the | communistmanifesto
entire bourgeois society.  In these crises a great part not only | communistmanifesto
of the existing products, but also of the previously created | communistmanifesto
productive forces, are periodically destroyed.  In these crises | communistmanifesto
there breaks out an epidemic that, in all earlier epochs, would | communistmanifesto
have seemed an absurdity--the epidemic of over-production. | communistmanifesto
Society suddenly finds itself put back into a state of momentary | communistmanifesto
barbarism; it appears as if a famine, a universal war of | communistmanifesto
devastation had cut off the supply of every means of subsistence; | communistmanifesto
industry and commerce seem to be destroyed; and why?  Because | communistmanifesto
there is too much civilisation, too much means of subsistence, | communistmanifesto
too much industry, too much commerce.  The productive forces at | communistmanifesto
the disposal of society no longer tend to further the development | communistmanifesto
of the conditions of bourgeois property; on the contrary, they | communistmanifesto
have become too powerful for these conditions, by which they are | communistmanifesto
fettered, and so soon as they overcome these fetters, they bring | communistmanifesto
disorder into the whole of bourgeois society, endanger the | communistmanifesto
existence of bourgeois property.  The conditions of bourgeois | communistmanifesto
society are too narrow to comprise the wealth created by them. | communistmanifesto
And how does the bourgeoisie get over these crises?  On the one | communistmanifesto
hand inforced destruction of a mass of productive forces; on the | communistmanifesto
other, by the conquest of new markets, and by the more thorough | communistmanifesto
exploitation of the old ones.  That is to say, by paving the | communistmanifesto
way for more extensive and more destructive crises, and by | communistmanifesto
diminishing the means whereby crises are prevented. | communistmanifesto
The weapons with which the bourgeoisie felled feudalism to the | communistmanifesto
ground are now turned against the bourgeoisie itself. | communistmanifesto
But not only has the bourgeoisie forged the weapons that bring | communistmanifesto
death to itself; it has also called into existence the men who | communistmanifesto
are to wield those weapons--the modern working class--the | communistmanifesto
proletarians. | communistmanifesto
In proportion as the bourgeoisie, i.e., capital, is developed, | communistmanifesto
in the same proportion is the proletariat, the modern working | communistmanifesto
class, developed--a class of labourers, who live only so long | communistmanifesto
as they find work, and who find work only so long as their labour | communistmanifesto
increases capital.  These labourers, who must sell themselves | communistmanifesto
piece-meal, are a commodity, like every other article of | communistmanifesto
commerce, and are consequently exposed to all the vicissitudes of | communistmanifesto
competition, to all the fluctuations of the market. | communistmanifesto
Owing to the extensive use of machinery and to division of | communistmanifesto
labour, the work of the proletarians has lost all individual | communistmanifesto
character, and consequently, all charm for the workman.  He | communistmanifesto
becomes an appendage of the machine, and it is only the most | communistmanifesto
simple, most monotonous, and most easily acquired knack, that is | communistmanifesto
required of him.  Hence, the cost of production of a workman is | communistmanifesto
restricted, almost entirely, to the means of subsistence that he | communistmanifesto
requires for his maintenance, and for the propagation of his | communistmanifesto
race.  But the price of a commodity, and therefore also of | communistmanifesto
labour, is equal to its cost of production.  In proportion | communistmanifesto
therefore, as the repulsiveness of the work increases, the wage | communistmanifesto
decreases.  Nay more, in proportion as the use of machinery and | communistmanifesto
division of labour increases, in the same proportion the burden | communistmanifesto
of toil also increases, whether by prolongation of the working | communistmanifesto
hours, by increase of the work exacted in a given time or by | communistmanifesto
increased speed of the machinery, etc. | communistmanifesto
Modern industry has converted the little workshop of the | communistmanifesto
patriarchal master into the great factory of the industrial | communistmanifesto
capitalist.  Masses of labourers, crowded into the factory, are | communistmanifesto
organised like soldiers.  As privates of the industrial army they | communistmanifesto
are placed under the command of a perfect hierarchy of officers | communistmanifesto
and sergeants.  Not only are they slaves of the bourgeois class, | communistmanifesto
and of the bourgeois State; they are daily and hourly enslaved by | communistmanifesto
the machine, by the over-looker, and, above all, by the | communistmanifesto
individual bourgeois manufacturer himself.  The more openly this | communistmanifesto
despotism proclaims gain to be its end and aim, the more petty, | communistmanifesto
the more hateful and the more embittering it is. | communistmanifesto
The less the skill and exertion of strength implied in manual | communistmanifesto
labour, in other words, the more modern industry becomes | communistmanifesto
developed, the more is the labour of men superseded by that of | communistmanifesto
women. Differences of age and sex have no longer any distinctive | communistmanifesto
social validity for the working class. All are instruments of | communistmanifesto
labour, more or less expensive to use, according to their age | communistmanifesto
and sex. | communistmanifesto
No sooner is the exploitation of the labourer by the manufacturer, | communistmanifesto
so far at an end, that he receives his wages in cash, than he is | communistmanifesto
set upon by the other portions of the bourgeoisie, the landlord, | communistmanifesto
the shopkeeper, the pawnbroker, etc. | communistmanifesto
The lower strata of the middle class--the small tradespeople, | communistmanifesto
shopkeepers, retired tradesmen generally, the handicraftsmen and | communistmanifesto
peasants--all these sink gradually into the proletariat, partly | communistmanifesto
because their diminutive capital does not suffice for the scale | communistmanifesto
on which Modern Industry is carried on, and is swamped in the | communistmanifesto
competition with the large capitalists, partly because their | communistmanifesto
specialized skill is rendered worthless by the new methods of | communistmanifesto
production.  Thus the proletariat is recruited from all classes | communistmanifesto
of the population. | communistmanifesto
The proletariat goes through various stages of development. | communistmanifesto
With its birth begins its struggle with the bourgeoisie.  At | communistmanifesto
first the contest is carried on by individual labourers, then by | communistmanifesto
the workpeople of a factory, then by the operatives of one trade, | communistmanifesto
in one locality, against the individual bourgeois who directly | communistmanifesto
exploits them.  They direct their attacks not against the | communistmanifesto
bourgeois conditions of production, but against the instruments | communistmanifesto
of production themselves; they destroy imported wares that | communistmanifesto
compete with their labour, they smash to pieces machinery, they | communistmanifesto
set factories ablaze, they seek to restore by force the vanished | communistmanifesto
status of the workman of the Middle Ages. | communistmanifesto
At this stage the labourers still form an incoherent mass | communistmanifesto
scattered over the whole country, and broken up by their mutual | communistmanifesto
competition.  If anywhere they unite to form more compact bodies, | communistmanifesto
this is not yet the consequence of their own active union, but of | communistmanifesto
the union of the bourgeoisie, which class, in order to attain its | communistmanifesto
own political ends, is compelled to set the whole proletariat in | communistmanifesto
motion, and is moreover yet, for a time, able to do so.  At this | communistmanifesto
stage, therefore, the proletarians do not fight their enemies, | communistmanifesto
but the enemies of their enemies, the remnants of absolute | communistmanifesto
monarchy, the landowners, the non-industrial bourgeois, the petty | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie.  Thus the whole historical movement is concentrated | communistmanifesto
in the hands of the bourgeoisie; every victory so obtained is a | communistmanifesto
victory for the bourgeoisie. | communistmanifesto
But with the development of industry the proletariat not only | communistmanifesto
increases in number; it becomes concentrated in greater masses, | communistmanifesto
its strength grows, and it feels that strength more.  The various | communistmanifesto
interests and conditions of life within the ranks of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat are more and more equalised, in proportion as | communistmanifesto
machinery obliterates all distinctions of labour, and nearly | communistmanifesto
everywhere reduces wages to the same low level.  The growing | communistmanifesto
competition among the bourgeois, and the resulting commercial | communistmanifesto
crises, make the wages of the workers ever more fluctuating.  The | communistmanifesto
unceasing improvement of machinery, ever more rapidly developing, | communistmanifesto
makes their livelihood more and more precarious; the collisions | communistmanifesto
between individual workmen and individual bourgeois take more and | communistmanifesto
more the character of collisions between two classes.  Thereupon | communistmanifesto
the workers begin to form combinations (Trades Unions) against | communistmanifesto
the bourgeois; they club together in order to keep up the rate of | communistmanifesto
wages; they found permanent associations in order to make | communistmanifesto
provision beforehand for these occasional revolts.  Here and | communistmanifesto
there the contest breaks out into riots. | communistmanifesto
Now and then the workers are victorious, but only for a time. | communistmanifesto
The real fruit of their battles lies, not in the immediate | communistmanifesto
result, but in the ever-expanding union of the workers.  This | communistmanifesto
union is helped on by the improved means of communication that | communistmanifesto
are created by modern industry and that place the workers of | communistmanifesto
different localities in contact with one another.  It was just | communistmanifesto
this contact that was needed to centralise the numerous local | communistmanifesto
struggles, all of the same character, into one national struggle | communistmanifesto
between classes.  But every class struggle is a political | communistmanifesto
struggle.  And that union, to attain which the burghers of the | communistmanifesto
Middle Ages, with their miserable highways, required centuries, | communistmanifesto
the modern proletarians, thanks to railways, achieve in a few | communistmanifesto
years. | communistmanifesto
This organisation of the proletarians into a class, and | communistmanifesto
consequently into a political party, is continually being upset | communistmanifesto
again by the competition between the workers themselves.  But it | communistmanifesto
ever rises up again, stronger, firmer, mightier.  It compels | communistmanifesto
legislative recognition of particular interests of the workers, | communistmanifesto
by taking advantage of the divisions among the bourgeoisie | communistmanifesto
itself.  Thus the ten-hours' bill in England was carried. | communistmanifesto
Altogether collisions between the classes of the old society | communistmanifesto
further, in many ways, the course of development of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat. The bourgeoisie finds itself involved in a constant | communistmanifesto
battle. At first with the aristocracy; later on, with those | communistmanifesto
portions of the bourgeoisie itself, whose interests have become | communistmanifesto
antagonistic to the progress of industry; at all times, with the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie of foreign countries. In all these battles it sees | communistmanifesto
itself compelled to appeal to the proletariat, to ask for its | communistmanifesto
help, and thus, to drag it into the political arena. The | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie itself, therefore, supplies the proletariat with its | communistmanifesto
own instruments of political and general education, in other | communistmanifesto
words, it furnishes the proletariat with weapons for fighting | communistmanifesto
the bourgeoisie. | communistmanifesto
Further, as we have already seen, entire sections of the ruling | communistmanifesto
classes are, by the advance of industry, precipitated into the | communistmanifesto
proletariat, or are at least threatened in their conditions of | communistmanifesto
existence.  These also supply the proletariat with fresh elements | communistmanifesto
of enlightenment and progress. | communistmanifesto
Finally, in times when the class struggle nears the decisive | communistmanifesto
hour, the process of dissolution going on within the ruling | communistmanifesto
class, in fact within the whole range of society, assumes such a | communistmanifesto
violent, glaring character, that a small section of the ruling | communistmanifesto
class cuts itself adrift, and joins the revolutionary class, the | communistmanifesto
class that holds the future in its hands.  Just as, therefore, at | communistmanifesto
an earlier period, a section of the nobility went over to the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie, so now a portion of the bourgeoisie goes over to the | communistmanifesto
proletariat, and in particular, a portion of the bourgeois | communistmanifesto
ideologists, who have raised themselves to the level of | communistmanifesto
comprehending theoretically the historical movement as a whole. | communistmanifesto
Of all the classes that stand face to face with the bourgeoisie | communistmanifesto
today, the proletariat alone is a really revolutionary class. | communistmanifesto
The other classes decay and finally disappear in the face of | communistmanifesto
Modern Industry; the proletariat is its special and essential | communistmanifesto
product.  The lower middle class, the small manufacturer, the | communistmanifesto
shopkeeper, the artisan, the peasant, all these fight against the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie, to save from extinction their existence as fractions | communistmanifesto
of the middle class.  They are therefore not revolutionary, but | communistmanifesto
conservative.  Nay more, they are reactionary, for they try | communistmanifesto
to roll back the wheel of history.  If by chance they are | communistmanifesto
revolutionary, they are so only in view of their impending | communistmanifesto
transfer into the proletariat, they thus defend not their | communistmanifesto
present, but their future interests, they desert their own | communistmanifesto
standpoint to place themselves at that of the proletariat. | communistmanifesto
The "dangerous class," the social scum, that passively rotting | communistmanifesto
mass thrown off by the lowest layers of old society, may, | communistmanifesto
here and there, be swept into the movement by a proletarian | communistmanifesto
revolution; its conditions of life, however, prepare it far more | communistmanifesto
for the part of a bribed tool of reactionary intrigue. | communistmanifesto
In the conditions of the proletariat, those of old society at | communistmanifesto
large are already virtually swamped.  The proletarian is without | communistmanifesto
property; his relation to his wife and children has no longer | communistmanifesto
anything in common with the bourgeois family-relations; modern | communistmanifesto
industrial labour, modern subjection to capital, the same in | communistmanifesto
England as in France, in America as in Germany, has stripped him | communistmanifesto
of every trace of national character.  Law, morality, religion, | communistmanifesto
are to him so many bourgeois prejudices, behind which lurk in | communistmanifesto
ambush just as many bourgeois interests. | communistmanifesto
All the preceding classes that got the upper hand, sought to | communistmanifesto
fortify their already acquired status by subjecting society at | communistmanifesto
large to their conditions of appropriation.  The proletarians | communistmanifesto
cannot become masters of the productive forces of society, except | communistmanifesto
by abolishing their own previous mode of appropriation, and | communistmanifesto
thereby also every other previous mode of appropriation.  They | communistmanifesto
have nothing of their own to secure and to fortify; their mission | communistmanifesto
is to destroy all previous securities for, and insurances of, | communistmanifesto
individual property. | communistmanifesto
All previous historical movements were movements of minorities, | communistmanifesto
or in the interests of minorities.  The proletarian movement is | communistmanifesto
the self-conscious, independent movement of the immense majority, | communistmanifesto
in the interests of the immense majority.  The proletariat, the | communistmanifesto
lowest stratum of our present society, cannot stir, cannot raise | communistmanifesto
itself up, without the whole superincumbent strata of official | communistmanifesto
society being sprung into the air. | communistmanifesto
Though not in substance, yet in form, the struggle of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat with the bourgeoisie is at first a national struggle. | communistmanifesto
The proletariat of each country must, of course, first of all | communistmanifesto
settle matters with its own bourgeoisie. | communistmanifesto
In depicting the most general phases of the development of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat, we traced the more or less veiled civil war, raging | communistmanifesto
within existing society, up to the point where that war breaks | communistmanifesto
out into open revolution, and where the violent overthrow of the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie lays the foundation for the sway of the proletariat. | communistmanifesto
Hitherto, every form of society has been based, as we have | communistmanifesto
already seen, on the antagonism of oppressing and oppressed | communistmanifesto
classes.  But in order to oppress a class, certain conditions | communistmanifesto
must be assured to it under which it can, at least, continue its | communistmanifesto
slavish existence.  The serf, in the period of serfdom, raised | communistmanifesto
himself to membership in the commune, just as the petty | communistmanifesto
bourgeois, under the yoke of feudal absolutism, managed to | communistmanifesto
develop into a bourgeois.  The modern laborer, on the contrary, | communistmanifesto
instead of rising with the progress of industry, sinks deeper and | communistmanifesto
deeper below the conditions of existence of his own class.  He | communistmanifesto
becomes a pauper, and pauperism develops more rapidly than | communistmanifesto
population and wealth.  And here it becomes evident, that the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie is unfit any longer to be the ruling class in | communistmanifesto
society, and to impose its conditions of existence upon society | communistmanifesto
as an over-riding law.  It is unfit to rule because it is | communistmanifesto
incompetent to assure an existence to its slave within his | communistmanifesto
slavery, because it cannot help letting him sink into such a | communistmanifesto
state, that it has to feed him, instead of being fed by him. | communistmanifesto
Society can no longer live under this bourgeoisie, in other | communistmanifesto
words, its existence is no longer compatible with society. | communistmanifesto
The essential condition for the existence, and for the sway of | communistmanifesto
the bourgeois class, is the formation and augmentation of | communistmanifesto
capital; the condition for capital is wage-labour.  Wage-labour | communistmanifesto
rests exclusively on competition between the laborers.  The | communistmanifesto
advance of industry, whose involuntary promoter is the bourgeoisie, | communistmanifesto
replaces the isolation of the labourers, due to competition, | communistmanifesto
by their revolutionary combination, due to association.  The | communistmanifesto
development of Modern Industry, therefore, cuts from under its | communistmanifesto
feet the very foundation on which the bourgeoisie produces and | communistmanifesto
appropriates products.  What the bourgeoisie, therefore, produces, | communistmanifesto
above all, is its own grave-diggers.  Its fall and the victory of | communistmanifesto
the proletariat are equally inevitable. | communistmanifesto
II.  PROLETARIANS AND COMMUNISTS | communistmanifesto
In what relation do the Communists stand to the proletarians as a | communistmanifesto
whole? | communistmanifesto
The Communists do not form a separate party opposed to other | communistmanifesto
working-class parties. | communistmanifesto
They have no interests separate and apart from those of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat as a whole. | communistmanifesto
They do not set up any sectarian principles of their own, | communistmanifesto
by which to shape and mould the proletarian movement. | communistmanifesto
The Communists are distinguished from the other working-class parties | communistmanifesto
by this only: (1) In the national struggles of the proletarians | communistmanifesto
of the different countries, they point out and bring to the front | communistmanifesto
the common interests of the entire proletariat, independently of | communistmanifesto
all nationality.  (2) In the various stages of development which the | communistmanifesto
struggle of the working class against the bourgeoisie has to pass | communistmanifesto
through, they always and everywhere represent the interests of the | communistmanifesto
movement as a whole. | communistmanifesto
The Communists, therefore, are on the one hand, practically, | communistmanifesto
the most advanced and resolute section of the working-class | communistmanifesto
parties of every country, that section which pushes forward | communistmanifesto
all others; on the other hand, theoretically, they have over | communistmanifesto
the great mass of the proletariat the advantage of clearly | communistmanifesto
understanding the line of march, the conditions, and the ultimate | communistmanifesto
general results of the proletarian movement. | communistmanifesto
The immediate aim of the Communist is the same as that of all | communistmanifesto
the other proletarian parties: formation of the proletariat into | communistmanifesto
a class, overthrow of the bourgeois supremacy, conquest of | communistmanifesto
political power by the proletariat. | communistmanifesto
The theoretical conclusions of the Communists are in no way | communistmanifesto
based on ideas or principles that have been invented, or | communistmanifesto
discovered, by this or that would-be universal reformer.  They | communistmanifesto
merely express, in general terms, actual relations springing from | communistmanifesto
an existing class struggle, from a historical movement going on | communistmanifesto
under our very eyes.  The abolition of existing property | communistmanifesto
relations is not at all a distinctive feature of Communism. | communistmanifesto
All property relations in the past have continually been subject | communistmanifesto
to historical change consequent upon the change in historical | communistmanifesto
conditions. | communistmanifesto
The French Revolution, for example, abolished feudal property in | communistmanifesto
favour of bourgeois property. | communistmanifesto
The distinguishing feature of Communism is not the abolition of | communistmanifesto
property generally, but the abolition of bourgeois property. But | communistmanifesto
modern bourgeois private property is the final and most complete | communistmanifesto
expression of the system of producing and appropriating products, | communistmanifesto
that is based on class antagonisms, on the exploitation of the | communistmanifesto
many by the few. | communistmanifesto
In this sense, the theory of the Communists may be summed up in | communistmanifesto
the single sentence: Abolition of private property. | communistmanifesto
We Communists have been reproached with the desire of abolishing | communistmanifesto
the right of personally acquiring property as the fruit of a | communistmanifesto
man's own labour, which property is alleged to be the groundwork | communistmanifesto
of all personal freedom, activity and independence. | communistmanifesto
Hard-won, self-acquired, self-earned property!  Do you mean the | communistmanifesto
property of the petty artisan and of the small peasant, a form of | communistmanifesto
property that preceded the bourgeois form?  There is no need to | communistmanifesto
abolish that; the development of industry has to a great extent | communistmanifesto
already destroyed it, and is still destroying it daily. | communistmanifesto
Or do you mean modern bourgeois private property? | communistmanifesto
But does wage-labour create any property for the labourer?  Not | communistmanifesto
a bit.  It creates capital, i.e., that kind of property which | communistmanifesto
exploits wage-labour, and which cannot increase except upon | communistmanifesto
condition of begetting a new supply of wage-labour for fresh | communistmanifesto
exploitation.  Property, in its present form, is based on the | communistmanifesto
antagonism of capital and wage-labour.  Let us examine both sides | communistmanifesto
of this antagonism. | communistmanifesto
To be a capitalist, is to have not only a purely personal, but a | communistmanifesto
social status in production.  Capital is a collective product, | communistmanifesto
and only by the united action of many members, nay, in the last | communistmanifesto
resort, only by the united action of all members of society, | communistmanifesto
can it be set in motion. | communistmanifesto
Capital is, therefore, not a personal, it is a social power. | communistmanifesto
When, therefore, capital is converted into common property, into | communistmanifesto
the property of all members of society, personal property is not | communistmanifesto
thereby transformed into social property. It is only the social | communistmanifesto
character of the property that is changed. It loses its | communistmanifesto
class-character. | communistmanifesto
Let us now take wage-labour. | communistmanifesto
The average price of wage-labour is the minimum wage, i.e., | communistmanifesto
that quantum of the means of subsistence, which is absolutely | communistmanifesto
requisite in bare existence as a labourer.  What, therefore, the | communistmanifesto
wage-labourer appropriates by means of his labour, merely | communistmanifesto
suffices to prolong and reproduce a bare existence.  We by no | communistmanifesto
means intend to abolish this personal appropriation of the | communistmanifesto
products of labour, an appropriation that is made for the | communistmanifesto
maintenance and reproduction of human life, and that leaves no | communistmanifesto
surplus wherewith to command the labour of others.  All that we | communistmanifesto
want to do away with, is the miserable character of this | communistmanifesto
appropriation, under which the labourer lives merely to increase | communistmanifesto
capital, and is allowed to live only in so far as the interest of | communistmanifesto
the ruling class requires it. | communistmanifesto
In bourgeois society, living labour is but a means to increase | communistmanifesto
accumulated labour.  In Communist society, accumulated labour | communistmanifesto
is but a means to widen, to enrich, to promote the existence | communistmanifesto
of the labourer. | communistmanifesto
In bourgeois society, therefore, the past dominates the present; | communistmanifesto
in Communist society, the present dominates the past.  In | communistmanifesto
bourgeois society capital is independent and has individuality, | communistmanifesto
while the living person is dependent and has no individuality. | communistmanifesto
And the abolition of this state of things is called by the | communistmanifesto
bourgeois, abolition of individuality and freedom! And rightly | communistmanifesto
so. The abolition of bourgeois individuality, bourgeois | communistmanifesto
independence, and bourgeois freedom is undoubtedly aimed at. | communistmanifesto
By freedom is meant, under the present bourgeois conditions of | communistmanifesto
production, free trade, free selling and buying. | communistmanifesto
But if selling and buying disappears, free selling and buying | communistmanifesto
disappears also.  This talk about free selling and buying, and | communistmanifesto
all the other "brave words" of our bourgeoisie about freedom in | communistmanifesto
general, have a meaning, if any, only in contrast with restricted | communistmanifesto
selling and buying, with the fettered traders of the Middle Ages, | communistmanifesto
but have no meaning when opposed to the Communistic abolition of | communistmanifesto
buying and selling, of the bourgeois conditions of production, | communistmanifesto
and of the bourgeoisie itself. | communistmanifesto
You are horrified at our intending to do away with private | communistmanifesto
property.  But in your existing society, private property is | communistmanifesto
already done away with for nine-tenths of the population; its | communistmanifesto
existence for the few is solely due to its non-existence in the | communistmanifesto
hands of those nine-tenths.  You reproach us, therefore, with | communistmanifesto
intending to do away with a form of property, the necessary | communistmanifesto
condition for whose existence is the non-existence of any | communistmanifesto
property for the immense majority of society. | communistmanifesto
In one word, you reproach us with intending to do away with your | communistmanifesto
property.  Precisely so; that is just what we intend. | communistmanifesto
From the moment when labour can no longer be converted into | communistmanifesto
capital, money, or rent, into a social power capable of being | communistmanifesto
monopolised, i.e., from the moment when individual property can | communistmanifesto
no longer be transformed into bourgeois property, into capital, | communistmanifesto
from that moment, you say individuality vanishes. | communistmanifesto
You must, therefore, confess that by "individual" you mean no | communistmanifesto
other person than the bourgeois, than the middle-class owner of | communistmanifesto
property.  This person must, indeed, be swept out of the way, and | communistmanifesto
made impossible. | communistmanifesto
Communism deprives no man of the power to appropriate the | communistmanifesto
products of society; all that it does is to deprive him of the | communistmanifesto
power to subjugate the labour of others by means of such | communistmanifesto
appropriation. | communistmanifesto
It has been objected that upon the abolition of private property | communistmanifesto
all work will cease, and universal laziness will overtake us. | communistmanifesto
According to this, bourgeois society ought long ago to have gone | communistmanifesto
to the dogs through sheer idleness; for those of its members who | communistmanifesto
work, acquire nothing, and those who acquire anything, do not | communistmanifesto
work. The whole of this objection is but another expression of | communistmanifesto
the tautology: that there can no longer be any wage-labour when | communistmanifesto
there is no longer any capital. | communistmanifesto
All objections urged against the Communistic mode of producing | communistmanifesto
and appropriating material products, have, in the same way, | communistmanifesto
been urged against the Communistic modes of producing and | communistmanifesto
appropriating intellectual products.  Just as, to the bourgeois, | communistmanifesto
the disappearance of class property is the disappearance of | communistmanifesto
production itself, so the disappearance of class culture is to | communistmanifesto
him identical with the disappearance of all culture. | communistmanifesto
That culture, the loss of which he laments, is, for the enormous | communistmanifesto
majority, a mere training to act as a machine. | communistmanifesto
But don't wrangle with us so long as you apply, to our intended | communistmanifesto
abolition of bourgeois property, the standard of your bourgeois | communistmanifesto
notions of freedom, culture, law, etc.  Your very ideas are but | communistmanifesto
the outgrowth of the conditions of your bourgeois production and | communistmanifesto
bourgeois property, just as your jurisprudence is but the will of | communistmanifesto
your class made into a law for all, a will, whose essential | communistmanifesto
character and direction are determined by the economical | communistmanifesto
conditions of existence of your class. | communistmanifesto
The selfish misconception that induces you to transform into | communistmanifesto
eternal laws of nature and of reason, the social forms | communistmanifesto
springing from your present mode of production and form of | communistmanifesto
property--historical relations that rise and disappear in the | communistmanifesto
progress of production--this misconception you share with every | communistmanifesto
ruling class that has preceded you.  What you see clearly in the | communistmanifesto
case of ancient property, what you admit in the case of feudal | communistmanifesto
property, you are of course forbidden to admit in the case of | communistmanifesto
your own bourgeois form of property. | communistmanifesto
Abolition of the family!  Even the most radical flare up at this | communistmanifesto
infamous proposal of the Communists. | communistmanifesto
On what foundation is the present family, the bourgeois family, | communistmanifesto
based?  On capital, on private gain.  In its completely developed | communistmanifesto
form this family exists only among the bourgeoisie.  But this | communistmanifesto
state of things finds its complement in the practical absence of | communistmanifesto
the family among the proletarians, and in public prostitution. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeois family will vanish as a matter of course when its | communistmanifesto
complement vanishes, and both will vanish with the vanishing of | communistmanifesto
capital. | communistmanifesto
Do you charge us with wanting to stop the exploitation of | communistmanifesto
children by their parents?  To this crime we plead guilty. | communistmanifesto
But, you will say, we destroy the most hallowed of relations, | communistmanifesto
when we replace home education by social. | communistmanifesto
And your education!  Is not that also social, and determined by the | communistmanifesto
social conditions under which you educate, by the intervention, | communistmanifesto
direct or indirect, of society, by means of schools, etc.?  The | communistmanifesto
Communists have not invented the intervention of society in | communistmanifesto
education; they do but seek to alter the character of that | communistmanifesto
intervention, and to rescue education from the influence of the | communistmanifesto
ruling class. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeois clap-trap about the family and education, about | communistmanifesto
the hallowed co-relation of parent and child, becomes all the | communistmanifesto
more disgusting, the more, by the action of Modern Industry, all | communistmanifesto
family ties among the proletarians are torn asunder, and their | communistmanifesto
children transformed into simple articles of commerce and | communistmanifesto
instruments of labour. | communistmanifesto
But you Communists would introduce community of women, screams | communistmanifesto
the whole bourgeoisie in chorus. | communistmanifesto
The bourgeois sees in his wife a mere instrument of production. | communistmanifesto
He hears that the instruments of production are to be exploited | communistmanifesto
in common, and, naturally, can come to no other conclusion than | communistmanifesto
that the lot of being common to all will likewise fall to the | communistmanifesto
women. | communistmanifesto
He has not even a suspicion that the real point is to do away | communistmanifesto
with the status of women as mere instruments of production. | communistmanifesto
For the rest, nothing is more ridiculous than the | communistmanifesto
virtuous indignation of our bourgeois at the community of women | communistmanifesto
which, they pretend, is to be openly and officially established | communistmanifesto
by the Communists.  The Communists have no need to introduce | communistmanifesto
community of women; it has existed almost from time immemorial. | communistmanifesto
Our bourgeois, not content with having the wives and daughters | communistmanifesto
of their proletarians at their disposal, not to speak of common | communistmanifesto
prostitutes, take the greatest pleasure in seducing each other's | communistmanifesto
wives. | communistmanifesto
Bourgeois marriage is in reality a system of wives in common | communistmanifesto
and thus, at the most, what the Communists might possibly | communistmanifesto
be reproached with, is that they desire to introduce, in | communistmanifesto
substitution for a hypocritically concealed, an openly legalised | communistmanifesto
community of women. For the rest, it is self-evident that the | communistmanifesto
abolition of the present system of production must bring with it | communistmanifesto
the abolition of the community of women springing from that | communistmanifesto
system, i.e., of prostitution both public and private. | communistmanifesto
The Communists are further reproached with desiring to abolish | communistmanifesto
countries and nationality. | communistmanifesto
The working men have no country.  We cannot take from them what | communistmanifesto
they have not got.  Since the proletariat must first of all | communistmanifesto
acquire political supremacy, must rise to be the leading class of | communistmanifesto
the nation, must constitute itself the nation, it is, so far, | communistmanifesto
itself national, though not in the bourgeois sense of the word. | communistmanifesto
National differences and antagonisms between peoples are daily | communistmanifesto
more and more vanishing, owing to the development of the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie, to freedom of commerce, to the world-market, to | communistmanifesto
uniformity in the mode of production and in the conditions of | communistmanifesto
life corresponding thereto. | communistmanifesto
The supremacy of the proletariat will cause them to vanish still | communistmanifesto
faster. United action, of the leading civilised countries at | communistmanifesto
least, is one of the first conditions for the emancipation of | communistmanifesto
the proletariat. | communistmanifesto
In proportion as the exploitation of one individual by another | communistmanifesto
is put an end to, the exploitation of one nation by another will | communistmanifesto
also be put an end to.  In proportion as the antagonism between | communistmanifesto
classes within the nation vanishes, the hostility of one nation | communistmanifesto
to another will come to an end. | communistmanifesto
The charges against Communism made from a religious, a | communistmanifesto
philosophical, and, generally, from an ideological standpoint, | communistmanifesto
are not deserving of serious examination. | communistmanifesto
Does it require deep intuition to comprehend that man's ideas, | communistmanifesto
views and conceptions, in one word, man's consciousness, changes | communistmanifesto
with every change in the conditions of his material existence, in | communistmanifesto
his social relations and in his social life? | communistmanifesto
What else does the history of ideas prove, than that | communistmanifesto
intellectual production changes its character in proportion as | communistmanifesto
material production is changed? The ruling ideas of each age | communistmanifesto
have ever been the ideas of its ruling class. | communistmanifesto
When people speak of ideas that revolutionise society, they do | communistmanifesto
but express the fact, that within the old society, the elements | communistmanifesto
of a new one have been created, and that the dissolution of the | communistmanifesto
old ideas keeps even pace with the dissolution of the old | communistmanifesto
conditions of existence. | communistmanifesto
When the ancient world was in its last throes, the ancient | communistmanifesto
religions were overcome by Christianity.  When Christian ideas | communistmanifesto
succumbed in the 18th century to rationalist ideas, feudal | communistmanifesto
society fought its death battle with the then revolutionary | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie.  The ideas of religious liberty and freedom of | communistmanifesto
conscience merely gave expression to the sway of free competition | communistmanifesto
within the domain of knowledge. | communistmanifesto
"Undoubtedly," it will be said, "religious, moral, philosophical | communistmanifesto
and juridical ideas have been modified in the course of | communistmanifesto
historical development.  But religion, morality philosophy, | communistmanifesto
political science, and law, constantly survived this change." | communistmanifesto
"There are, besides, eternal truths, such as Freedom, Justice, | communistmanifesto
etc. that are common to all states of society. But Communism | communistmanifesto
abolishes eternal truths, it abolishes all religion, and all | communistmanifesto
morality, instead of constituting them on a new basis; it | communistmanifesto
therefore acts in contradiction to all past historical experience." | communistmanifesto
What does this accusation reduce itself to?  The history of | communistmanifesto
all past society has consisted in the development of class | communistmanifesto
antagonisms, antagonisms that assumed different forms at | communistmanifesto
different epochs. | communistmanifesto
But whatever form they may have taken, one fact is common to all | communistmanifesto
past ages, viz., the exploitation of one part of society by the | communistmanifesto
other. No wonder, then, that the social consciousness of past | communistmanifesto
ages, despite all the multiplicity and variety it displays, | communistmanifesto
moves within certain common forms, or general ideas, which | communistmanifesto
cannot completely vanish except with the total disappearance of | communistmanifesto
class antagonisms. | communistmanifesto
The Communist revolution is the most radical rupture with | communistmanifesto
traditional property relations; no wonder that its development | communistmanifesto
involves the most radical rupture with traditional ideas. | communistmanifesto
But let us have done with the bourgeois objections to Communism. | communistmanifesto
We have seen above, that the first step in the revolution by the | communistmanifesto
working class, is to raise the proletariat to the position of | communistmanifesto
ruling as to win the battle of democracy. | communistmanifesto
The proletariat will use its political supremacy to wrest, by | communistmanifesto
degrees, all capital from the bourgeoisie, to centralise all | communistmanifesto
instruments of production in the hands of the State, i.e., of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat organised as the ruling class; and to increase the | communistmanifesto
total of productive forces as rapidly as possible. | communistmanifesto
Of course, in the beginning, this cannot be effected except by | communistmanifesto
means of despotic inroads on the rights of property, and on | communistmanifesto
the conditions of bourgeois production; by means of measures, | communistmanifesto
therefore, which appear economically insufficient and untenable, | communistmanifesto
but which, in the course of the movement, outstrip themselves, | communistmanifesto
necessitate further inroads upon the old social order, and are | communistmanifesto
unavoidable as a means of entirely revolutionising the mode of | communistmanifesto
production. | communistmanifesto
These measures will of course be different in different | communistmanifesto
countries. | communistmanifesto
Nevertheless in the most advanced countries, the following will | communistmanifesto
be pretty generally applicable. | communistmanifesto
1.  Abolition of property in land and application of all rents | communistmanifesto
    of land to public purposes. | communistmanifesto
2.  A heavy progressive or graduated income tax. | communistmanifesto
3.  Abolition of all right of inheritance. | communistmanifesto
4.  Confiscation of the property of all emigrants and rebels. | communistmanifesto
5.  Centralisation of credit in the hands of the State, by means | communistmanifesto
    of a national bank with State capital and an exclusive | communistmanifesto
    monopoly. | communistmanifesto
6.  Centralisation of the means of communication and transport | communistmanifesto
    in the hands of the State. | communistmanifesto
7.  Extension of factories and instruments of production owned by | communistmanifesto
    the State; the bringing into cultivation of waste-lands, and | communistmanifesto
    the improvement of the soil generally in accordance with a | communistmanifesto
    common plan. | communistmanifesto
8.  Equal liability of all to labour.  Establishment of | communistmanifesto
    industrial armies, especially for agriculture. | communistmanifesto
9.  Combination of agriculture with manufacturing industries; | communistmanifesto
    gradual abolition of the distinction between town and | communistmanifesto
    country, by a more equable distribution of the population | communistmanifesto
    over the country. | communistmanifesto
10. Free education for all children in public schools. | communistmanifesto
    Abolition of children's factory labour in its present form. | communistmanifesto
    Combination of education with industrial production, &c., &c. | communistmanifesto
When, in the course of development, class distinctions have | communistmanifesto
disappeared, and all production has been concentrated in the | communistmanifesto
hands of a vast association of the whole nation, the public power | communistmanifesto
will lose its political character.  Political power, properly so | communistmanifesto
called, is merely the organised power of one class for oppressing | communistmanifesto
another.  If the proletariat during its contest with the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie is compelled, by the force of circumstances, to | communistmanifesto
organise itself as a class, if, by means of a revolution, it | communistmanifesto
makes itself the ruling class, and, as such, sweeps away by force | communistmanifesto
the old conditions of production, then it will, along with these | communistmanifesto
conditions, have swept away the conditions for the existence of | communistmanifesto
class antagonisms and of classes generally, and will thereby have | communistmanifesto
abolished its own supremacy as a class. | communistmanifesto
In place of the old bourgeois society, with its classes and | communistmanifesto
class antagonisms, we shall have an association, in which | communistmanifesto
the free development of each is the condition for the free | communistmanifesto
development of all. | communistmanifesto
III.  SOCIALIST AND COMMUNIST LITERATURE | communistmanifesto
1. REACTIONARY SOCIALISM | communistmanifesto
A. Feudal Socialism | communistmanifesto
Owing to their historical position, it became the vocation of the | communistmanifesto
aristocracies of France and England to write pamphlets against | communistmanifesto
modern bourgeois society.  In the French revolution of July 1830, | communistmanifesto
and in the English reform agitation, these aristocracies again | communistmanifesto
succumbed to the hateful upstart.  Thenceforth, a serious political | communistmanifesto
contest was altogether out of the question.  A literary battle | communistmanifesto
alone remained possible.  But even in the domain of literature | communistmanifesto
the old cries of the restoration period had become impossible. | communistmanifesto
In order to arouse sympathy, the aristocracy were obliged to | communistmanifesto
lose sight, apparently, of their own interests, and to formulate | communistmanifesto
their indictment against the bourgeoisie in the interest of the | communistmanifesto
exploited working class alone.  Thus the aristocracy took their | communistmanifesto
revenge by singing lampoons on their new master, and whispering | communistmanifesto
in his ears sinister prophecies of coming catastrophe. | communistmanifesto
In this way arose Feudal Socialism: half lamentation, half | communistmanifesto
lampoon; half echo of the past, half menace of the future; at | communistmanifesto
times, by its bitter, witty and incisive criticism, striking the | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie to the very heart's core; but always ludicrous in | communistmanifesto
its effect, through total incapacity to comprehend the march of | communistmanifesto
modern history. | communistmanifesto
The aristocracy, in order to rally the people to them, waved the | communistmanifesto
proletarian alms-bag in front for a banner.  But the people, so | communistmanifesto
often as it joined them, saw on their hindquarters the old feudal | communistmanifesto
coats of arms, and deserted with loud and irreverent laughter. | communistmanifesto
One section of the French Legitimists and "Young England" | communistmanifesto
exhibited this spectacle. | communistmanifesto
In pointing out that their mode of exploitation was different to | communistmanifesto
that of the bourgeoisie, the feudalists forget that they | communistmanifesto
exploited under circumstances and conditions that were quite | communistmanifesto
different, and that are now antiquated.  In showing that, under | communistmanifesto
their rule, the modern proletariat never existed, they forget | communistmanifesto
that the modern bourgeoisie is the necessary offspring of their | communistmanifesto
own form of society. | communistmanifesto
For the rest, so little do they conceal the reactionary | communistmanifesto
character of their criticism that their chief accusation against | communistmanifesto
the bourgeoisie amounts to this, that under the bourgeois regime | communistmanifesto
a class is being developed, which is destined to cut up root and | communistmanifesto
branch the old order of society. | communistmanifesto
What they upbraid the bourgeoisie with is not so much that it | communistmanifesto
creates a proletariat, as that it creates a revolutionary | communistmanifesto
proletariat. | communistmanifesto
In political practice, therefore, they join in all coercive | communistmanifesto
measures against the working class; and in ordinary life, | communistmanifesto
despite their high falutin phrases, they stoop to pick up the | communistmanifesto
golden apples dropped from the tree of industry, and to barter | communistmanifesto
truth, love, and honour for traffic in wool, beetroot-sugar, and | communistmanifesto
potato spirits. | communistmanifesto
As the parson has ever gone hand in hand with the landlord, | communistmanifesto
so has Clerical Socialism with Feudal Socialism. | communistmanifesto
Nothing is easier than to give Christian asceticism a Socialist | communistmanifesto
tinge. Has not Christianity declaimed against private property, | communistmanifesto
against marriage, against the State? Has it not preached in the | communistmanifesto
place of these, charity and poverty, celibacy and mortification | communistmanifesto
of the flesh, monastic life and Mother Church? Christian | communistmanifesto
Socialism is but the holy, water with which the priest consecrates | communistmanifesto
the heart-burnings of the aristocrat. | communistmanifesto
B. Petty-Bourgeois Socialism | communistmanifesto
The feudal aristocracy was not the only class that was ruined by | communistmanifesto
the bourgeoisie, not the only class whose conditions of existence | communistmanifesto
pined and perished in the atmosphere of modern bourgeois society. | communistmanifesto
The mediaeval burgesses and the small peasant proprietors were | communistmanifesto
the precursors of the modern bourgeoisie.  In those countries | communistmanifesto
which are but little developed, industrially and commercially, | communistmanifesto
these two classes still vegetate side by side with the rising | communistmanifesto
bourgeoisie. | communistmanifesto
In countries where modern civilisation has become fully | communistmanifesto
developed, a new class of petty bourgeois has been formed, | communistmanifesto
fluctuating between proletariat and bourgeoisie and ever renewing | communistmanifesto
itself as a supplementary part of bourgeois society.  The | communistmanifesto
individual members of this class, however, are being constantly | communistmanifesto
hurled down into the proletariat by the action of competition, | communistmanifesto
and, as modern industry develops, they even see the moment | communistmanifesto
approaching when they will completely disappear as an independent | communistmanifesto
section of modern society, to be replaced, in manufactures, | communistmanifesto
agriculture and commerce, by overlookers, bailiffs and shopmen. | communistmanifesto
In countries like France, where the peasants constitute far more | communistmanifesto
than half of the population, it was natural that writers who | communistmanifesto
sided with the proletariat against the bourgeoisie, should use, | communistmanifesto
in their criticism of the bourgeois regime, the standard of the | communistmanifesto
peasant and petty bourgeois, and from the standpoint of these | communistmanifesto
intermediate classes should take up the cudgels for the working | communistmanifesto
class.  Thus arose petty-bourgeois Socialism.  Sismondi was the | communistmanifesto
head of this school, not only in France but also in England. | communistmanifesto
This school of Socialism dissected with great acuteness the | communistmanifesto
contradictions in the conditions of modern production.  It laid | communistmanifesto
bare the hypocritical apologies of economists.  It proved, | communistmanifesto
incontrovertibly, the disastrous effects of machinery and | communistmanifesto
division of labour; the concentration of capital and land in a | communistmanifesto
few hands; overproduction and crises; it pointed out the | communistmanifesto
inevitable ruin of the petty bourgeois and peasant, the misery | communistmanifesto
of the proletariat, the anarchy in production, the crying | communistmanifesto
inequalities in the distribution of wealth, the industrial war of | communistmanifesto
extermination between nations, the dissolution of old moral | communistmanifesto
bonds, of the old family relations, of the old nationalities. | communistmanifesto
In its positive aims, however, this form of Socialism aspires | communistmanifesto
either to restoring the old means of production and of exchange, | communistmanifesto
and with them the old property relations, and the old society, or | communistmanifesto
to cramping the modern means of production and of exchange, | communistmanifesto
within the framework of the old property relations that have | communistmanifesto
been, and were bound to be, exploded by those means.  In either | communistmanifesto
case, it is both reactionary and Utopian. | communistmanifesto
Its last words are: corporate guilds for manufacture, | communistmanifesto
patriarchal relations in agriculture. | communistmanifesto
Ultimately, when stubborn historical facts had dispersed all | communistmanifesto
intoxicating effects of self-deception, this form of Socialism | communistmanifesto
ended in a miserable fit of the blues. | communistmanifesto
C. German, or "True," Socialism | communistmanifesto
The Socialist and Communist literature of France, a literature | communistmanifesto
that originated under the pressure of a bourgeoisie in power, and | communistmanifesto
that was the expression of the struggle against this power, was | communistmanifesto
introduced into Germany at a time when the bourgeoisie, in that | communistmanifesto
country, had just begun its contest with feudal absolutism. | communistmanifesto
German philosophers, would-be philosophers, and beaux esprits, | communistmanifesto
eagerly seized on this literature, only forgetting, that when | communistmanifesto
these writings immigrated from France into Germany, French social | communistmanifesto
conditions had not immigrated along with them.  In contact with | communistmanifesto
German social conditions, this French literature lost all its | communistmanifesto
immediate practical significance, and assumed a purely literary | communistmanifesto
aspect.  Thus, to the German philosophers of the eighteenth | communistmanifesto
century, the demands of the first French Revolution were nothing | communistmanifesto
more than the demands of "Practical Reason" in general, and the | communistmanifesto
utterance of the will of the revolutionary French bourgeoisie | communistmanifesto
signified in their eyes the law of pure Will, of Will as it was | communistmanifesto
bound to be, of true human Will generally. | communistmanifesto
The world of the German literate consisted solely in bringing | communistmanifesto
the new French ideas into harmony with their ancient philosophical | communistmanifesto
conscience, or rather, in annexing the French ideas without | communistmanifesto
deserting their own philosophic point of view. | communistmanifesto
This annexation took place in the same way in which a foreign | communistmanifesto
language is appropriated, namely, by translation. | communistmanifesto
It is well known how the monks wrote silly lives of Catholic | communistmanifesto
Saints over the manuscripts on which the classical works of | communistmanifesto
ancient heathendom had been written.  The German literate | communistmanifesto
reversed this process with the profane French literature.  They | communistmanifesto
wrote their philosophical nonsense beneath the French original. | communistmanifesto
For instance, beneath the French criticism of the economic | communistmanifesto
functions of money, they wrote "Alienation of Humanity," and | communistmanifesto
beneath the French criticism of the bourgeois State they wrote | communistmanifesto
"dethronement of the Category of the General," and so forth. | communistmanifesto
The introduction of these philosophical phrases at the back of | communistmanifesto
the French historical criticisms they dubbed "Philosophy of | communistmanifesto
Action," "True Socialism," "German Science of Socialism," | communistmanifesto
"Philosophical Foundation of Socialism," and so on. | communistmanifesto
The French Socialist and Communist literature was thus completely | communistmanifesto
emasculated. And, since it ceased in the hands of the German to express | communistmanifesto
the struggle of one class with the other, he felt conscious of having | communistmanifesto
overcome "French one-sidedness" and of representing, not true | communistmanifesto
requirements, but the requirements of truth; not the interests of the | communistmanifesto
proletariat, but the interests of Human Nature, of Man in general, who | communistmanifesto
belongs to no class, has no reality, who exists only in the misty realm | communistmanifesto
of philosophical fantasy. | communistmanifesto
This German Socialism, which took its schoolboy task so seriously | communistmanifesto
and solemnly, and extolled its poor stock-in-trade in such | communistmanifesto
mountebank fashion, meanwhile gradually lost its pedantic | communistmanifesto
innocence. | communistmanifesto
The fight of the German, and especially, of the Prussian bourgeoisie, | communistmanifesto
against feudal aristocracy and absolute monarchy, in other words, the | communistmanifesto
liberal movement, became more earnest. | communistmanifesto
                  [_As given in the original edition_.] | gulliverstravels
The author of these Travels, Mr. Lemuel Gulliver, is my ancient and | gulliverstravels
intimate friend; there is likewise some relation between us on the | gulliverstravels
mother’s side.  About three years ago, Mr. Gulliver growing weary of the | gulliverstravels
concourse of curious people coming to him at his house in Redriff, made a | gulliverstravels
small purchase of land, with a convenient house, near Newark, in | gulliverstravels
Nottinghamshire, his native country; where he now lives retired, yet in | gulliverstravels
good esteem among his neighbours. | gulliverstravels
Although Mr. Gulliver was born in Nottinghamshire, where his father | gulliverstravels
dwelt, yet I have heard him say his family came from Oxfordshire; to | gulliverstravels
confirm which, I have observed in the churchyard at Banbury in that | gulliverstravels
