county, several tombs and monuments of the Gullivers. | gulliverstravels
Before he quitted Redriff, he left the custody of the following papers in | gulliverstravels
my hands, with the liberty to dispose of them as I should think fit.  I | gulliverstravels
have carefully perused them three times.  The style is very plain and | gulliverstravels
simple; and the only fault I find is, that the author, after the manner | gulliverstravels
of travellers, is a little too circumstantial.  There is an air of truth | gulliverstravels
apparent through the whole; and indeed the author was so distinguished | gulliverstravels
for his veracity, that it became a sort of proverb among his neighbours | gulliverstravels
at Redriff, when any one affirmed a thing, to say, it was as true as if | gulliverstravels
Mr. Gulliver had spoken it. | gulliverstravels
By the advice of several worthy persons, to whom, with the author’s | gulliverstravels
permission, I communicated these papers, I now venture to send them into | gulliverstravels
the world, hoping they may be, at least for some time, a better | gulliverstravels
entertainment to our young noblemen, than the common scribbles of | gulliverstravels
politics and party. | gulliverstravels
This volume would have been at least twice as large, if I had not made | gulliverstravels
bold to strike out innumerable passages relating to the winds and tides, | gulliverstravels
as well as to the variations and bearings in the several voyages, | gulliverstravels
together with the minute descriptions of the management of the ship in | gulliverstravels
storms, in the style of sailors; likewise the account of longitudes and | gulliverstravels
latitudes; wherein I have reason to apprehend, that Mr. Gulliver may be a | gulliverstravels
little dissatisfied.  But I was resolved to fit the work as much as | gulliverstravels
possible to the general capacity of readers.  However, if my own | gulliverstravels
ignorance in sea affairs shall have led me to commit some mistakes, I | gulliverstravels
alone am answerable for them.  And if any traveller hath a curiosity to | gulliverstravels
see the whole work at large, as it came from the hands of the author, I | gulliverstravels
will be ready to gratify him. | gulliverstravels
As for any further particulars relating to the author, the reader will | gulliverstravels
receive satisfaction from the first pages of the book. | gulliverstravels
                                                          RICHARD SYMPSON. | gulliverstravels
A LETTER FROM CAPTAIN GULLIVER TO HIS COUSIN SYMPSON. | gulliverstravels
                        WRITTEN IN THE YEAR 1727. | gulliverstravels
I hope you will be ready to own publicly, whenever you shall be called to | gulliverstravels
it, that by your great and frequent urgency you prevailed on me to | gulliverstravels
publish a very loose and uncorrect account of my travels, with directions | gulliverstravels
to hire some young gentleman of either university to put them in order, | gulliverstravels
and correct the style, as my cousin Dampier did, by my advice, in his | gulliverstravels
book called “A Voyage round the world.”  But I do not remember I gave you | gulliverstravels
power to consent that any thing should be omitted, and much less that any | gulliverstravels
thing should be inserted; therefore, as to the latter, I do here renounce | gulliverstravels
every thing of that kind; particularly a paragraph about her majesty | gulliverstravels
Queen Anne, of most pious and glorious memory; although I did reverence | gulliverstravels
and esteem her more than any of human species.  But you, or your | gulliverstravels
interpolator, ought to have considered, that it was not my inclination, | gulliverstravels
so was it not decent to praise any animal of our composition before my | gulliverstravels
master _Houyhnhnm_: And besides, the fact was altogether false; for to my | gulliverstravels
knowledge, being in England during some part of her majesty’s reign, she | gulliverstravels
did govern by a chief minister; nay even by two successively, the first | gulliverstravels
whereof was the lord of Godolphin, and the second the lord of Oxford; so | gulliverstravels
that you have made me say the thing that was not.  Likewise in the | gulliverstravels
account of the academy of projectors, and several passages of my | gulliverstravels
discourse to my master _Houyhnhnm_, you have either omitted some material | gulliverstravels
circumstances, or minced or changed them in such a manner, that I do | gulliverstravels
hardly know my own work.  When I formerly hinted to you something of this | gulliverstravels
in a letter, you were pleased to answer that you were afraid of giving | gulliverstravels
offence; that people in power were very watchful over the press, and apt | gulliverstravels
not only to interpret, but to punish every thing which looked like an | gulliverstravels
_innuendo_ (as I think you call it).  But, pray how could that which I | gulliverstravels
spoke so many years ago, and at about five thousand leagues distance, in | gulliverstravels
another reign, be applied to any of the _Yahoos_, who now are said to | gulliverstravels
govern the herd; especially at a time when I little thought, or feared, | gulliverstravels
the unhappiness of living under them?  Have not I the most reason to | gulliverstravels
complain, when I see these very _Yahoos_ carried by _Houyhnhnms_ in a | gulliverstravels
vehicle, as if they were brutes, and those the rational creatures?  And | gulliverstravels
indeed to avoid so monstrous and detestable a sight was one principal | gulliverstravels
motive of my retirement hither. | gulliverstravels
Thus much I thought proper to tell you in relation to yourself, and to | gulliverstravels
the trust I reposed in you. | gulliverstravels
I do, in the next place, complain of my own great want of judgment, in | gulliverstravels
being prevailed upon by the entreaties and false reasoning of you and | gulliverstravels
some others, very much against my own opinion, to suffer my travels to be | gulliverstravels
published.  Pray bring to your mind how often I desired you to consider, | gulliverstravels
when you insisted on the motive of public good, that the _Yahoos_ were a | gulliverstravels
species of animals utterly incapable of amendment by precept or example: | gulliverstravels
and so it has proved; for, instead of seeing a full stop put to all | gulliverstravels
abuses and corruptions, at least in this little island, as I had reason | gulliverstravels
to expect; behold, after above six months warning, I cannot learn that my | gulliverstravels
book has produced one single effect according to my intentions.  I | gulliverstravels
desired you would let me know, by a letter, when party and faction were | gulliverstravels
extinguished; judges learned and upright; pleaders honest and modest, | gulliverstravels
with some tincture of common sense, and Smithfield blazing with pyramids | gulliverstravels
of law books; the young nobility’s education entirely changed; the | gulliverstravels
physicians banished; the female _Yahoos_ abounding in virtue, honour, | gulliverstravels
truth, and good sense; courts and levees of great ministers thoroughly | gulliverstravels
weeded and swept; wit, merit, and learning rewarded; all disgracers of | gulliverstravels
the press in prose and verse condemned to eat nothing but their own | gulliverstravels
cotton, and quench their thirst with their own ink.  These, and a | gulliverstravels
thousand other reformations, I firmly counted upon by your encouragement; | gulliverstravels
as indeed they were plainly deducible from the precepts delivered in my | gulliverstravels
book.  And it must be owned, that seven months were a sufficient time to | gulliverstravels
correct every vice and folly to which _Yahoos_ are subject, if their | gulliverstravels
natures had been capable of the least disposition to virtue or wisdom. | gulliverstravels
Yet, so far have you been from answering my expectation in any of your | gulliverstravels
letters; that on the contrary you are loading our carrier every week with | gulliverstravels
libels, and keys, and reflections, and memoirs, and second parts; wherein | gulliverstravels
I see myself accused of reflecting upon great state folk; of degrading | gulliverstravels
human nature (for so they have still the confidence to style it), and of | gulliverstravels
abusing the female sex.  I find likewise that the writers of those | gulliverstravels
bundles are not agreed among themselves; for some of them will not allow | gulliverstravels
me to be the author of my own travels; and others make me author of books | gulliverstravels
to which I am wholly a stranger. | gulliverstravels
I find likewise that your printer has been so careless as to confound the | gulliverstravels
times, and mistake the dates, of my several voyages and returns; neither | gulliverstravels
assigning the true year, nor the true month, nor day of the month: and I | gulliverstravels
hear the original manuscript is all destroyed since the publication of my | gulliverstravels
book; neither have I any copy left: however, I have sent you some | gulliverstravels
corrections, which you may insert, if ever there should be a second | gulliverstravels
edition: and yet I cannot stand to them; but shall leave that matter to | gulliverstravels
my judicious and candid readers to adjust it as they please. | gulliverstravels
I hear some of our sea _Yahoos_ find fault with my sea-language, as not | gulliverstravels
proper in many parts, nor now in use.  I cannot help it.  In my first | gulliverstravels
voyages, while I was young, I was instructed by the oldest mariners, and | gulliverstravels
learned to speak as they did.  But I have since found that the sea | gulliverstravels
_Yahoos_ are apt, like the land ones, to become new-fangled in their | gulliverstravels
words, which the latter change every year; insomuch, as I remember upon | gulliverstravels
each return to my own country their old dialect was so altered, that I | gulliverstravels
could hardly understand the new.  And I observe, when any _Yahoo_ comes | gulliverstravels
from London out of curiosity to visit me at my house, we neither of us | gulliverstravels
are able to deliver our conceptions in a manner intelligible to the | gulliverstravels
other. | gulliverstravels
If the censure of the _Yahoos_ could any way affect me, I should have | gulliverstravels
great reason to complain, that some of them are so bold as to think my | gulliverstravels
book of travels a mere fiction out of mine own brain, and have gone so | gulliverstravels
far as to drop hints, that the _Houyhnhnms_ and _Yahoos_ have no more | gulliverstravels
existence than the inhabitants of Utopia. | gulliverstravels
Indeed I must confess, that as to the people of _Lilliput_, _Brobdingrag_ | gulliverstravels
(for so the word should have been spelt, and not erroneously | gulliverstravels
_Brobdingnag_), and _Laputa_, I have never yet heard of any _Yahoo_ so | gulliverstravels
presumptuous as to dispute their being, or the facts I have related | gulliverstravels
concerning them; because the truth immediately strikes every reader with | gulliverstravels
conviction.  And is there less probability in my account of the | gulliverstravels
_Houyhnhnms_ or _Yahoos_, when it is manifest as to the latter, there are | gulliverstravels
so many thousands even in this country, who only differ from their | gulliverstravels
brother brutes in _Houyhnhnmland_, because they use a sort of jabber, and | gulliverstravels
do not go naked?  I wrote for their amendment, and not their approbation. | gulliverstravels
The united praise of the whole race would be of less consequence to me, | gulliverstravels
than the neighing of those two degenerate _Houyhnhnms_ I keep in my | gulliverstravels
stable; because from these, degenerate as they are, I still improve in | gulliverstravels
some virtues without any mixture of vice. | gulliverstravels
Do these miserable animals presume to think, that I am so degenerated as | gulliverstravels
to defend my veracity?  _Yahoo_ as I am, it is well known through all | gulliverstravels
_Houyhnhnmland_, that, by the instructions and example of my illustrious | gulliverstravels
master, I was able in the compass of two years (although I confess with | gulliverstravels
the utmost difficulty) to remove that infernal habit of lying, shuffling, | gulliverstravels
deceiving, and equivocating, so deeply rooted in the very souls of all my | gulliverstravels
species; especially the Europeans. | gulliverstravels
I have other complaints to make upon this vexatious occasion; but I | gulliverstravels
forbear troubling myself or you any further.  I must freely confess, that | gulliverstravels
since my last return, some corruptions of my _Yahoo_ nature have revived | gulliverstravels
in me by conversing with a few of your species, and particularly those of | gulliverstravels
my own family, by an unavoidable necessity; else I should never have | gulliverstravels
attempted so absurd a project as that of reforming the _Yahoo_ race in | gulliverstravels
this kingdom: But I have now done with all such visionary schemes for | gulliverstravels
ever. | gulliverstravels
_April_ 2, 1727 | gulliverstravels
PART I.  A VOYAGE TO LILLIPUT. | gulliverstravels
CHAPTER I. | gulliverstravels
The author gives some account of himself and family.  His first | gulliverstravels
inducements to travel.  He is shipwrecked, and swims for his life.  Gets | gulliverstravels
safe on shore in the country of Lilliput; is made a prisoner, and carried | gulliverstravels
up the country. | gulliverstravels
My father had a small estate in Nottinghamshire: I was the third of five | gulliverstravels
sons.  He sent me to Emanuel College in Cambridge at fourteen years old, | gulliverstravels
where I resided three years, and applied myself close to my studies; but | gulliverstravels
the charge of maintaining me, although I had a very scanty allowance, | gulliverstravels
being too great for a narrow fortune, I was bound apprentice to Mr. James | gulliverstravels
Bates, an eminent surgeon in London, with whom I continued four years. | gulliverstravels
My father now and then sending me small sums of money, I laid them out in | gulliverstravels
learning navigation, and other parts of the mathematics, useful to those | gulliverstravels
who intend to travel, as I always believed it would be, some time or | gulliverstravels
other, my fortune to do.  When I left Mr. Bates, I went down to my | gulliverstravels
father: where, by the assistance of him and my uncle John, and some other | gulliverstravels
relations, I got forty pounds, and a promise of thirty pounds a year to | gulliverstravels
maintain me at Leyden: there I studied physic two years and seven months, | gulliverstravels
knowing it would be useful in long voyages. | gulliverstravels
Soon after my return from Leyden, I was recommended by my good master, | gulliverstravels
Mr. Bates, to be surgeon to the Swallow, Captain Abraham Pannel, | gulliverstravels
commander; with whom I continued three years and a half, making a voyage | gulliverstravels
or two into the Levant, and some other parts.  When I came back I | gulliverstravels
resolved to settle in London; to which Mr. Bates, my master, encouraged | gulliverstravels
me, and by him I was recommended to several patients.  I took part of a | gulliverstravels
small house in the Old Jewry; and being advised to alter my condition, I | gulliverstravels
married Mrs. Mary Burton, second daughter to Mr. Edmund Burton, hosier, | gulliverstravels
in Newgate-street, with whom I received four hundred pounds for a | gulliverstravels
portion. | gulliverstravels
But my good master Bates dying in two years after, and I having few | gulliverstravels
friends, my business began to fail; for my conscience would not suffer me | gulliverstravels
to imitate the bad practice of too many among my brethren.  Having | gulliverstravels
therefore consulted with my wife, and some of my acquaintance, I | gulliverstravels
determined to go again to sea.  I was surgeon successively in two ships, | gulliverstravels
and made several voyages, for six years, to the East and West Indies, by | gulliverstravels
which I got some addition to my fortune.  My hours of leisure I spent in | gulliverstravels
reading the best authors, ancient and modern, being always provided with | gulliverstravels
a good number of books; and when I was ashore, in observing the manners | gulliverstravels
and dispositions of the people, as well as learning their language; | gulliverstravels
wherein I had a great facility, by the strength of my memory. | gulliverstravels
The last of these voyages not proving very fortunate, I grew weary of the | gulliverstravels
sea, and intended to stay at home with my wife and family.  I removed | gulliverstravels
from the Old Jewry to Fetter Lane, and from thence to Wapping, hoping to | gulliverstravels
get business among the sailors; but it would not turn to account.  After | gulliverstravels
three years expectation that things would mend, I accepted an | gulliverstravels
advantageous offer from Captain William Prichard, master of the Antelope, | gulliverstravels
who was making a voyage to the South Sea.  We set sail from Bristol, May | gulliverstravels
4, 1699, and our voyage was at first very prosperous. | gulliverstravels
It would not be proper, for some reasons, to trouble the reader with the | gulliverstravels
particulars of our adventures in those seas; let it suffice to inform | gulliverstravels
him, that in our passage from thence to the East Indies, we were driven | gulliverstravels
by a violent storm to the north-west of Van Diemen’s Land.  By an | gulliverstravels
observation, we found ourselves in the latitude of 30 degrees 2 minutes | gulliverstravels
south.  Twelve of our crew were dead by immoderate labour and ill food; | gulliverstravels
the rest were in a very weak condition.  On the 5th of November, which | gulliverstravels
was the beginning of summer in those parts, the weather being very hazy, | gulliverstravels
the seamen spied a rock within half a cable’s length of the ship; but the | gulliverstravels
wind was so strong, that we were driven directly upon it, and immediately | gulliverstravels
split.  Six of the crew, of whom I was one, having let down the boat into | gulliverstravels
the sea, made a shift to get clear of the ship and the rock.  We rowed, | gulliverstravels
by my computation, about three leagues, till we were able to work no | gulliverstravels
longer, being already spent with labour while we were in the ship.  We | gulliverstravels
therefore trusted ourselves to the mercy of the waves, and in about half | gulliverstravels
an hour the boat was overset by a sudden flurry from the north.  What | gulliverstravels
became of my companions in the boat, as well as of those who escaped on | gulliverstravels
the rock, or were left in the vessel, I cannot tell; but conclude they | gulliverstravels
were all lost.  For my own part, I swam as fortune directed me, and was | gulliverstravels
pushed forward by wind and tide.  I often let my legs drop, and could | gulliverstravels
feel no bottom; but when I was almost gone, and able to struggle no | gulliverstravels
longer, I found myself within my depth; and by this time the storm was | gulliverstravels
much abated.  The declivity was so small, that I walked near a mile | gulliverstravels
before I got to the shore, which I conjectured was about eight o’clock in | gulliverstravels
the evening.  I then advanced forward near half a mile, but could not | gulliverstravels
discover any sign of houses or inhabitants; at least I was in so weak a | gulliverstravels
condition, that I did not observe them.  I was extremely tired, and with | gulliverstravels
that, and the heat of the weather, and about half a pint of brandy that I | gulliverstravels
drank as I left the ship, I found myself much inclined to sleep.  I lay | gulliverstravels
down on the grass, which was very short and soft, where I slept sounder | gulliverstravels
than ever I remembered to have done in my life, and, as I reckoned, about | gulliverstravels
nine hours; for when I awaked, it was just day-light.  I attempted to | gulliverstravels
rise, but was not able to stir: for, as I happened to lie on my back, I | gulliverstravels
found my arms and legs were strongly fastened on each side to the ground; | gulliverstravels
and my hair, which was long and thick, tied down in the same manner.  I | gulliverstravels
likewise felt several slender ligatures across my body, from my arm-pits | gulliverstravels
to my thighs.  I could only look upwards; the sun began to grow hot, and | gulliverstravels
the light offended my eyes.  I heard a confused noise about me; but in | gulliverstravels
the posture I lay, could see nothing except the sky.  In a little time I | gulliverstravels
felt something alive moving on my left leg, which advancing gently | gulliverstravels
forward over my breast, came almost up to my chin; when, bending my eyes | gulliverstravels
downwards as much as I could, I perceived it to be a human creature not | gulliverstravels
six inches high, with a bow and arrow in his hands, and a quiver at his | gulliverstravels
back.  In the mean time, I felt at least forty more of the same kind (as | gulliverstravels
I conjectured) following the first.  I was in the utmost astonishment, | gulliverstravels
and roared so loud, that they all ran back in a fright; and some of them, | gulliverstravels
as I was afterwards told, were hurt with the falls they got by leaping | gulliverstravels
from my sides upon the ground.  However, they soon returned, and one of | gulliverstravels
them, who ventured so far as to get a full sight of my face, lifting up | gulliverstravels
his hands and eyes by way of admiration, cried out in a shrill but | gulliverstravels
distinct voice, _Hekinah degul_: the others repeated the same words | gulliverstravels
several times, but then I knew not what they meant.  I lay all this | gulliverstravels
while, as the reader may believe, in great uneasiness.  At length, | gulliverstravels
struggling to get loose, I had the fortune to break the strings, and | gulliverstravels
wrench out the pegs that fastened my left arm to the ground; for, by | gulliverstravels
lifting it up to my face, I discovered the methods they had taken to bind | gulliverstravels
me, and at the same time with a violent pull, which gave me excessive | gulliverstravels
pain, I a little loosened the strings that tied down my hair on the left | gulliverstravels
side, so that I was just able to turn my head about two inches.  But the | gulliverstravels
creatures ran off a second time, before I could seize them; whereupon | gulliverstravels
there was a great shout in a very shrill accent, and after it ceased I | gulliverstravels
heard one of them cry aloud _Tolgo phonac_; when in an instant I felt | gulliverstravels
above a hundred arrows discharged on my left hand, which, pricked me like | gulliverstravels
so many needles; and besides, they shot another flight into the air, as | gulliverstravels
we do bombs in Europe, whereof many, I suppose, fell on my body, (though | gulliverstravels
I felt them not), and some on my face, which I immediately covered with | gulliverstravels
my left hand.  When this shower of arrows was over, I fell a groaning | gulliverstravels
with grief and pain; and then striving again to get loose, they | gulliverstravels
discharged another volley larger than the first, and some of them | gulliverstravels
attempted with spears to stick me in the sides; but by good luck I had on | gulliverstravels
a buff jerkin, which they could not pierce.  I thought it the most | gulliverstravels
prudent method to lie still, and my design was to continue so till night, | gulliverstravels
when, my left hand being already loose, I could easily free myself: and | gulliverstravels
as for the inhabitants, I had reason to believe I might be a match for | gulliverstravels
the greatest army they could bring against me, if they were all of the | gulliverstravels
same size with him that I saw.  But fortune disposed otherwise of me. | gulliverstravels
When the people observed I was quiet, they discharged no more arrows; | gulliverstravels
but, by the noise I heard, I knew their numbers increased; and about four | gulliverstravels
yards from me, over against my right ear, I heard a knocking for above an | gulliverstravels
hour, like that of people at work; when turning my head that way, as well | gulliverstravels
as the pegs and strings would permit me, I saw a stage erected about a | gulliverstravels
foot and a half from the ground, capable of holding four of the | gulliverstravels
inhabitants, with two or three ladders to mount it: from whence one of | gulliverstravels
them, who seemed to be a person of quality, made me a long speech, | gulliverstravels
whereof I understood not one syllable.  But I should have mentioned, that | gulliverstravels
before the principal person began his oration, he cried out three times, | gulliverstravels
_Langro dehul san_ (these words and the former were afterwards repeated | gulliverstravels
and explained to me); whereupon, immediately, about fifty of the | gulliverstravels
inhabitants came and cut the strings that fastened the left side of my | gulliverstravels
head, which gave me the liberty of turning it to the right, and of | gulliverstravels
observing the person and gesture of him that was to speak.  He appeared | gulliverstravels
to be of a middle age, and taller than any of the other three who | gulliverstravels
attended him, whereof one was a page that held up his train, and seemed | gulliverstravels
to be somewhat longer than my middle finger; the other two stood one on | gulliverstravels
each side to support him.  He acted every part of an orator, and I could | gulliverstravels
observe many periods of threatenings, and others of promises, pity, and | gulliverstravels
kindness.  I answered in a few words, but in the most submissive manner, | gulliverstravels
lifting up my left hand, and both my eyes to the sun, as calling him for | gulliverstravels
a witness; and being almost famished with hunger, having not eaten a | gulliverstravels
morsel for some hours before I left the ship, I found the demands of | gulliverstravels
nature so strong upon me, that I could not forbear showing my impatience | gulliverstravels
(perhaps against the strict rules of decency) by putting my finger | gulliverstravels
frequently to my mouth, to signify that I wanted food.  The _hurgo_ (for | gulliverstravels
so they call a great lord, as I afterwards learnt) understood me very | gulliverstravels
well.  He descended from the stage, and commanded that several ladders | gulliverstravels
should be applied to my sides, on which above a hundred of the | gulliverstravels
inhabitants mounted and walked towards my mouth, laden with baskets full | gulliverstravels
of meat, which had been provided and sent thither by the king’s orders, | gulliverstravels
upon the first intelligence he received of me.  I observed there was the | gulliverstravels
flesh of several animals, but could not distinguish them by the taste. | gulliverstravels
There were shoulders, legs, and loins, shaped like those of mutton, and | gulliverstravels
very well dressed, but smaller than the wings of a lark.  I ate them by | gulliverstravels
two or three at a mouthful, and took three loaves at a time, about the | gulliverstravels
bigness of musket bullets.  They supplied me as fast as they could, | gulliverstravels
showing a thousand marks of wonder and astonishment at my bulk and | gulliverstravels
appetite.  I then made another sign, that I wanted drink.  They found by | gulliverstravels
my eating that a small quantity would not suffice me; and being a most | gulliverstravels
ingenious people, they slung up, with great dexterity, one of their | gulliverstravels
largest hogsheads, then rolled it towards my hand, and beat out the top; | gulliverstravels
I drank it off at a draught, which I might well do, for it did not hold | gulliverstravels
half a pint, and tasted like a small wine of Burgundy, but much more | gulliverstravels
delicious.  They brought me a second hogshead, which I drank in the same | gulliverstravels
manner, and made signs for more; but they had none to give me.  When I | gulliverstravels
had performed these wonders, they shouted for joy, and danced upon my | gulliverstravels
breast, repeating several times as they did at first, _Hekinah degul_. | gulliverstravels
They made me a sign that I should throw down the two hogsheads, but first | gulliverstravels
warning the people below to stand out of the way, crying aloud, _Borach | gulliverstravels
mevolah_; and when they saw the vessels in the air, there was a universal | gulliverstravels
shout of _Hekinah degul_.  I confess I was often tempted, while they were | gulliverstravels
passing backwards and forwards on my body, to seize forty or fifty of the | gulliverstravels
first that came in my reach, and dash them against the ground.  But the | gulliverstravels
remembrance of what I had felt, which probably might not be the worst | gulliverstravels
they could do, and the promise of honour I made them—for so I interpreted | gulliverstravels
my submissive behaviour—soon drove out these imaginations.  Besides, I | gulliverstravels
now considered myself as bound by the laws of hospitality, to a people | gulliverstravels
who had treated me with so much expense and magnificence.  However, in my | gulliverstravels
thoughts I could not sufficiently wonder at the intrepidity of these | gulliverstravels
diminutive mortals, who durst venture to mount and walk upon my body, | gulliverstravels
while one of my hands was at liberty, without trembling at the very sight | gulliverstravels
of so prodigious a creature as I must appear to them.  After some time, | gulliverstravels
when they observed that I made no more demands for meat, there appeared | gulliverstravels
before me a person of high rank from his imperial majesty.  His | gulliverstravels
excellency, having mounted on the small of my right leg, advanced | gulliverstravels
forwards up to my face, with about a dozen of his retinue; and producing | gulliverstravels
his credentials under the signet royal, which he applied close to my | gulliverstravels
eyes, spoke about ten minutes without any signs of anger, but with a kind | gulliverstravels
of determinate resolution, often pointing forwards, which, as I | gulliverstravels
afterwards found, was towards the capital city, about half a mile | gulliverstravels
distant; whither it was agreed by his majesty in council that I must be | gulliverstravels
conveyed.  I answered in few words, but to no purpose, and made a sign | gulliverstravels
with my hand that was loose, putting it to the other (but over his | gulliverstravels
excellency’s head for fear of hurting him or his train) and then to my | gulliverstravels
own head and body, to signify that I desired my liberty.  It appeared | gulliverstravels
that he understood me well enough, for he shook his head by way of | gulliverstravels
disapprobation, and held his hand in a posture to show that I must be | gulliverstravels
carried as a prisoner.  However, he made other signs to let me understand | gulliverstravels
that I should have meat and drink enough, and very good treatment. | gulliverstravels
Whereupon I once more thought of attempting to break my bonds; but again, | gulliverstravels
when I felt the smart of their arrows upon my face and hands, which were | gulliverstravels
all in blisters, and many of the darts still sticking in them, and | gulliverstravels
observing likewise that the number of my enemies increased, I gave tokens | gulliverstravels
to let them know that they might do with me what they pleased.  Upon | gulliverstravels
this, the _hurgo_ and his train withdrew, with much civility and cheerful | gulliverstravels
countenances.  Soon after I heard a general shout, with frequent | gulliverstravels
repetitions of the words _Peplom selan_; and I felt great numbers of | gulliverstravels
people on my left side relaxing the cords to such a degree, that I was | gulliverstravels
able to turn upon my right, and to ease myself with making water; which I | gulliverstravels
very plentifully did, to the great astonishment of the people; who, | gulliverstravels
conjecturing by my motion what I was going to do, immediately opened to | gulliverstravels
the right and left on that side, to avoid the torrent, which fell with | gulliverstravels
such noise and violence from me.  But before this, they had daubed my | gulliverstravels
face and both my hands with a sort of ointment, very pleasant to the | gulliverstravels
smell, which, in a few minutes, removed all the smart of their arrows. | gulliverstravels
These circumstances, added to the refreshment I had received by their | gulliverstravels
victuals and drink, which were very nourishing, disposed me to sleep.  I | gulliverstravels
slept about eight hours, as I was afterwards assured; and it was no | gulliverstravels
wonder, for the physicians, by the emperor’s order, had mingled a sleepy | gulliverstravels
potion in the hogsheads of wine. | gulliverstravels
It seems, that upon the first moment I was discovered sleeping on the | gulliverstravels
ground, after my landing, the emperor had early notice of it by an | gulliverstravels
express; and determined in council, that I should be tied in the manner I | gulliverstravels
have related, (which was done in the night while I slept;) that plenty of | gulliverstravels
meat and drink should be sent to me, and a machine prepared to carry me | gulliverstravels
to the capital city. | gulliverstravels
This resolution perhaps may appear very bold and dangerous, and I am | gulliverstravels
confident would not be imitated by any prince in Europe on the like | gulliverstravels
occasion.  However, in my opinion, it was extremely prudent, as well as | gulliverstravels
generous: for, supposing these people had endeavoured to kill me with | gulliverstravels
their spears and arrows, while I was asleep, I should certainly have | gulliverstravels
awaked with the first sense of smart, which might so far have roused my | gulliverstravels
rage and strength, as to have enabled me to break the strings wherewith I | gulliverstravels
was tied; after which, as they were not able to make resistance, so they | gulliverstravels
could expect no mercy. | gulliverstravels
These people are most excellent mathematicians, and arrived to a great | gulliverstravels
perfection in mechanics, by the countenance and encouragement of the | gulliverstravels
emperor, who is a renowned patron of learning.  This prince has several | gulliverstravels
machines fixed on wheels, for the carriage of trees and other great | gulliverstravels
weights.  He often builds his largest men of war, whereof some are nine | gulliverstravels
feet long, in the woods where the timber grows, and has them carried on | gulliverstravels
these engines three or four hundred yards to the sea.  Five hundred | gulliverstravels
carpenters and engineers were immediately set at work to prepare the | gulliverstravels
greatest engine they had.  It was a frame of wood raised three inches | gulliverstravels
from the ground, about seven feet long, and four wide, moving upon | gulliverstravels
twenty-two wheels.  The shout I heard was upon the arrival of this | gulliverstravels
engine, which, it seems, set out in four hours after my landing.  It was | gulliverstravels
brought parallel to me, as I lay.  But the principal difficulty was to | gulliverstravels
raise and place me in this vehicle.  Eighty poles, each of one foot high, | gulliverstravels
were erected for this purpose, and very strong cords, of the bigness of | gulliverstravels
packthread, were fastened by hooks to many bandages, which the workmen | gulliverstravels
had girt round my neck, my hands, my body, and my legs.  Nine hundred of | gulliverstravels
the strongest men were employed to draw up these cords, by many pulleys | gulliverstravels
fastened on the poles; and thus, in less than three hours, I was raised | gulliverstravels
and slung into the engine, and there tied fast.  All this I was told; | gulliverstravels
for, while the operation was performing, I lay in a profound sleep, by | gulliverstravels
the force of that soporiferous medicine infused into my liquor.  Fifteen | gulliverstravels
hundred of the emperor’s largest horses, each about four inches and a | gulliverstravels
half high, were employed to draw me towards the metropolis, which, as I | gulliverstravels
said, was half a mile distant. | gulliverstravels
About four hours after we began our journey, I awaked by a very | gulliverstravels
ridiculous accident; for the carriage being stopped a while, to adjust | gulliverstravels
something that was out of order, two or three of the young natives had | gulliverstravels
the curiosity to see how I looked when I was asleep; they climbed up into | gulliverstravels
the engine, and advancing very softly to my face, one of them, an officer | gulliverstravels
in the guards, put the sharp end of his half-pike a good way up into my | gulliverstravels
left nostril, which tickled my nose like a straw, and made me sneeze | gulliverstravels
violently; whereupon they stole off unperceived, and it was three weeks | gulliverstravels
before I knew the cause of my waking so suddenly.  We made a long march | gulliverstravels
the remaining part of the day, and, rested at night with five hundred | gulliverstravels
guards on each side of me, half with torches, and half with bows and | gulliverstravels
arrows, ready to shoot me if I should offer to stir.  The next morning at | gulliverstravels
sun-rise we continued our march, and arrived within two hundred yards of | gulliverstravels
the city gates about noon.  The emperor, and all his court, came out to | gulliverstravels
meet us; but his great officers would by no means suffer his majesty to | gulliverstravels
endanger his person by mounting on my body. | gulliverstravels
At the place where the carriage stopped there stood an ancient temple, | gulliverstravels
esteemed to be the largest in the whole kingdom; which, having been | gulliverstravels
polluted some years before by an unnatural murder, was, according to the | gulliverstravels
zeal of those people, looked upon as profane, and therefore had been | gulliverstravels
applied to common use, and all the ornaments and furniture carried away. | gulliverstravels
In this edifice it was determined I should lodge.  The great gate | gulliverstravels
fronting to the north was about four feet high, and almost two feet wide, | gulliverstravels
through which I could easily creep.  On each side of the gate was a small | gulliverstravels
window, not above six inches from the ground: into that on the left side, | gulliverstravels
the king’s smith conveyed fourscore and eleven chains, like those that | gulliverstravels
hang to a lady’s watch in Europe, and almost as large, which were locked | gulliverstravels
to my left leg with six-and-thirty padlocks.  Over against this temple, | gulliverstravels
on the other side of the great highway, at twenty feet distance, there | gulliverstravels
was a turret at least five feet high.  Here the emperor ascended, with | gulliverstravels
many principal lords of his court, to have an opportunity of viewing me, | gulliverstravels
as I was told, for I could not see them.  It was reckoned that above a | gulliverstravels
hundred thousand inhabitants came out of the town upon the same errand; | gulliverstravels
and, in spite of my guards, I believe there could not be fewer than ten | gulliverstravels
thousand at several times, who mounted my body by the help of ladders. | gulliverstravels
But a proclamation was soon issued, to forbid it upon pain of death. | gulliverstravels
When the workmen found it was impossible for me to break loose, they cut | gulliverstravels
all the strings that bound me; whereupon I rose up, with as melancholy a | gulliverstravels
disposition as ever I had in my life.  But the noise and astonishment of | gulliverstravels
the people, at seeing me rise and walk, are not to be expressed.  The | gulliverstravels
chains that held my left leg were about two yards long, and gave me not | gulliverstravels
only the liberty of walking backwards and forwards in a semicircle, but, | gulliverstravels
being fixed within four inches of the gate, allowed me to creep in, and | gulliverstravels
lie at my full length in the temple. | gulliverstravels
CHAPTER II. | gulliverstravels
The emperor of Lilliput, attended by several of the nobility, comes to | gulliverstravels
see the author in his confinement.  The emperor’s person and habit | gulliverstravels
described.  Learned men appointed to teach the author their language.  He | gulliverstravels
gains favour by his mild disposition.  His pockets are searched, and his | gulliverstravels
sword and pistols taken from him. | gulliverstravels
When I found myself on my feet, I looked about me, and must confess I | gulliverstravels
never beheld a more entertaining prospect.  The country around appeared | gulliverstravels
like a continued garden, and the enclosed fields, which were generally | gulliverstravels
forty feet square, resembled so many beds of flowers.  These fields were | gulliverstravels
intermingled with woods of half a stang, {301} and the tallest trees, as | gulliverstravels
I could judge, appeared to be seven feet high.  I viewed the town on my | gulliverstravels
left hand, which looked like the painted scene of a city in a theatre. | gulliverstravels
I had been for some hours extremely pressed by the necessities of nature; | gulliverstravels
which was no wonder, it being almost two days since I had last | gulliverstravels
disburdened myself.  I was under great difficulties between urgency and | gulliverstravels
shame.  The best expedient I could think of, was to creep into my house, | gulliverstravels
which I accordingly did; and shutting the gate after me, I went as far as | gulliverstravels
the length of my chain would suffer, and discharged my body of that | gulliverstravels
uneasy load.  But this was the only time I was ever guilty of so | gulliverstravels
uncleanly an action; for which I cannot but hope the candid reader will | gulliverstravels
give some allowance, after he has maturely and impartially considered my | gulliverstravels
case, and the distress I was in.  From this time my constant practice | gulliverstravels
was, as soon as I rose, to perform that business in open air, at the full | gulliverstravels
extent of my chain; and due care was taken every morning before company | gulliverstravels
came, that the offensive matter should be carried off in wheel-barrows, | gulliverstravels
by two servants appointed for that purpose.  I would not have dwelt so | gulliverstravels
long upon a circumstance that, perhaps, at first sight, may appear not | gulliverstravels
very momentous, if I had not thought it necessary to justify my | gulliverstravels
character, in point of cleanliness, to the world; which, I am told, some | gulliverstravels
of my maligners have been pleased, upon this and other occasions, to call | gulliverstravels
in question. | gulliverstravels
When this adventure was at an end, I came back out of my house, having | gulliverstravels
occasion for fresh air.  The emperor was already descended from the | gulliverstravels
tower, and advancing on horseback towards me, which had like to have cost | gulliverstravels
him dear; for the beast, though very well trained, yet wholly unused to | gulliverstravels
such a sight, which appeared as if a mountain moved before him, reared up | gulliverstravels
on its hinder feet: but that prince, who is an excellent horseman, kept | gulliverstravels
his seat, till his attendants ran in, and held the bridle, while his | gulliverstravels
majesty had time to dismount.  When he alighted, he surveyed me round | gulliverstravels
with great admiration; but kept beyond the length of my chain.  He | gulliverstravels
ordered his cooks and butlers, who were already prepared, to give me | gulliverstravels
victuals and drink, which they pushed forward in a sort of vehicles upon | gulliverstravels
wheels, till I could reach them.  I took these vehicles and soon emptied | gulliverstravels
them all; twenty of them were filled with meat, and ten with liquor; each | gulliverstravels
of the former afforded me two or three good mouthfuls; and I emptied the | gulliverstravels
liquor of ten vessels, which was contained in earthen vials, into one | gulliverstravels
vehicle, drinking it off at a draught; and so I did with the rest.  The | gulliverstravels
empress, and young princes of the blood of both sexes, attended by many | gulliverstravels
ladies, sat at some distance in their chairs; but upon the accident that | gulliverstravels
happened to the emperor’s horse, they alighted, and came near his person, | gulliverstravels
which I am now going to describe.  He is taller by almost the breadth of | gulliverstravels
my nail, than any of his court; which alone is enough to strike an awe | gulliverstravels
into the beholders.  His features are strong and masculine, with an | gulliverstravels
Austrian lip and arched nose, his complexion olive, his countenance | gulliverstravels
erect, his body and limbs well proportioned, all his motions graceful, | gulliverstravels
and his deportment majestic.  He was then past his prime, being | gulliverstravels
twenty-eight years and three quarters old, of which he had reigned about | gulliverstravels
seven in great felicity, and generally victorious.  For the better | gulliverstravels
convenience of beholding him, I lay on my side, so that my face was | gulliverstravels
parallel to his, and he stood but three yards off: however, I have had | gulliverstravels
him since many times in my hand, and therefore cannot be deceived in the | gulliverstravels
description.  His dress was very plain and simple, and the fashion of it | gulliverstravels
between the Asiatic and the European; but he had on his head a light | gulliverstravels
helmet of gold, adorned with jewels, and a plume on the crest.  He held | gulliverstravels
his sword drawn in his hand to defend himself, if I should happen to | gulliverstravels
break loose; it was almost three inches long; the hilt and scabbard were | gulliverstravels
gold enriched with diamonds.  His voice was shrill, but very clear and | gulliverstravels
articulate; and I could distinctly hear it when I stood up.  The ladies | gulliverstravels
and courtiers were all most magnificently clad; so that the spot they | gulliverstravels
stood upon seemed to resemble a petticoat spread upon the ground, | gulliverstravels
embroidered with figures of gold and silver.  His imperial majesty spoke | gulliverstravels
often to me, and I returned answers: but neither of us could understand a | gulliverstravels
syllable.  There were several of his priests and lawyers present (as I | gulliverstravels
conjectured by their habits), who were commanded to address themselves to | gulliverstravels
me; and I spoke to them in as many languages as I had the least | gulliverstravels
smattering of, which were High and Low Dutch, Latin, French, Spanish, | gulliverstravels
Italian, and Lingua Franca, but all to no purpose.  After about two hours | gulliverstravels
the court retired, and I was left with a strong guard, to prevent the | gulliverstravels
impertinence, and probably the malice of the rabble, who were very | gulliverstravels
impatient to crowd about me as near as they durst; and some of them had | gulliverstravels
the impudence to shoot their arrows at me, as I sat on the ground by the | gulliverstravels
door of my house, whereof one very narrowly missed my left eye.  But the | gulliverstravels
colonel ordered six of the ringleaders to be seized, and thought no | gulliverstravels
punishment so proper as to deliver them bound into my hands; which some | gulliverstravels
of his soldiers accordingly did, pushing them forward with the butt-ends | gulliverstravels
of their pikes into my reach.  I took them all in my right hand, put five | gulliverstravels
of them into my coat-pocket; and as to the sixth, I made a countenance as | gulliverstravels
if I would eat him alive.  The poor man squalled terribly, and the | gulliverstravels
colonel and his officers were in much pain, especially when they saw me | gulliverstravels
take out my penknife: but I soon put them out of fear; for, looking | gulliverstravels
mildly, and immediately cutting the strings he was bound with, I set him | gulliverstravels
gently on the ground, and away he ran.  I treated the rest in the same | gulliverstravels
manner, taking them one by one out of my pocket; and I observed both the | gulliverstravels
soldiers and people were highly delighted at this mark of my clemency, | gulliverstravels
which was represented very much to my advantage at court. | gulliverstravels
Towards night I got with some difficulty into my house, where I lay on | gulliverstravels
the ground, and continued to do so about a fortnight; during which time, | gulliverstravels
the emperor gave orders to have a bed prepared for me.  Six hundred beds | gulliverstravels
of the common measure were brought in carriages, and worked up in my | gulliverstravels
house; a hundred and fifty of their beds, sewn together, made up the | gulliverstravels
breadth and length; and these were four double: which, however, kept me | gulliverstravels
but very indifferently from the hardness of the floor, that was of smooth | gulliverstravels
stone.  By the same computation, they provided me with sheets, blankets, | gulliverstravels
and coverlets, tolerable enough for one who had been so long inured to | gulliverstravels
hardships. | gulliverstravels
As the news of my arrival spread through the kingdom, it brought | gulliverstravels
prodigious numbers of rich, idle, and curious people to see me; so that | gulliverstravels
the villages were almost emptied; and great neglect of tillage and | gulliverstravels
household affairs must have ensued, if his imperial majesty had not | gulliverstravels
provided, by several proclamations and orders of state, against this | gulliverstravels
inconveniency.  He directed that those who had already beheld me should | gulliverstravels
return home, and not presume to come within fifty yards of my house, | gulliverstravels
without license from the court; whereby the secretaries of state got | gulliverstravels
considerable fees. | gulliverstravels
In the mean time the emperor held frequent councils, to debate what | gulliverstravels
course should be taken with me; and I was afterwards assured by a | gulliverstravels
particular friend, a person of great quality, who was as much in the | gulliverstravels
secret as any, that the court was under many difficulties concerning me. | gulliverstravels
They apprehended my breaking loose; that my diet would be very expensive, | gulliverstravels
and might cause a famine.  Sometimes they determined to starve me; or at | gulliverstravels
least to shoot me in the face and hands with poisoned arrows, which would | gulliverstravels
soon despatch me; but again they considered, that the stench of so large | gulliverstravels
a carcass might produce a plague in the metropolis, and probably spread | gulliverstravels
through the whole kingdom.  In the midst of these consultations, several | gulliverstravels
officers of the army went to the door of the great council-chamber, and | gulliverstravels
two of them being admitted, gave an account of my behaviour to the six | gulliverstravels
criminals above-mentioned; which made so favourable an impression in the | gulliverstravels
breast of his majesty and the whole board, in my behalf, that an imperial | gulliverstravels
commission was issued out, obliging all the villages, nine hundred yards | gulliverstravels
round the city, to deliver in every morning six beeves, forty sheep, and | gulliverstravels
other victuals for my sustenance; together with a proportionable quantity | gulliverstravels
of bread, and wine, and other liquors; for the due payment of which, his | gulliverstravels
majesty gave assignments upon his treasury:—for this prince lives chiefly | gulliverstravels
upon his own demesnes; seldom, except upon great occasions, raising any | gulliverstravels
subsidies upon his subjects, who are bound to attend him in his wars at | gulliverstravels
their own expense.  An establishment was also made of six hundred persons | gulliverstravels
to be my domestics, who had board-wages allowed for their maintenance, | gulliverstravels
and tents built for them very conveniently on each side of my door.  It | gulliverstravels
was likewise ordered, that three hundred tailors should make me a suit of | gulliverstravels
clothes, after the fashion of the country; that six of his majesty’s | gulliverstravels
greatest scholars should be employed to instruct me in their language; | gulliverstravels
and lastly, that the emperor’s horses, and those of the nobility and | gulliverstravels
troops of guards, should be frequently exercised in my sight, to accustom | gulliverstravels
themselves to me.  All these orders were duly put in execution; and in | gulliverstravels
about three weeks I made a great progress in learning their language; | gulliverstravels
during which time the emperor frequently honoured me with his visits, and | gulliverstravels
was pleased to assist my masters in teaching me.  We began already to | gulliverstravels
converse together in some sort; and the first words I learnt, were to | gulliverstravels
express my desire “that he would please give me my liberty;” which I | gulliverstravels
every day repeated on my knees.  His answer, as I could comprehend it, | gulliverstravels
was, “that this must be a work of time, not to be thought on without the | gulliverstravels
advice of his council, and that first I must _lumos kelmin pesso desmar | gulliverstravels
lon emposo_;” that is, swear a peace with him and his kingdom.  However, | gulliverstravels
that I should be used with all kindness.  And he advised me to “acquire, | gulliverstravels
by my patience and discreet behaviour, the good opinion of himself and | gulliverstravels
his subjects.”  He desired “I would not take it ill, if he gave orders to | gulliverstravels
certain proper officers to search me; for probably I might carry about me | gulliverstravels
several weapons, which must needs be dangerous things, if they answered | gulliverstravels
the bulk of so prodigious a person.”  I said, “His majesty should be | gulliverstravels
satisfied; for I was ready to strip myself, and turn up my pockets before | gulliverstravels
him.”  This I delivered part in words, and part in signs.  He replied, | gulliverstravels
“that, by the laws of the kingdom, I must be searched by two of his | gulliverstravels
officers; that he knew this could not be done without my consent and | gulliverstravels
assistance; and he had so good an opinion of my generosity and justice, | gulliverstravels
as to trust their persons in my hands; that whatever they took from me, | gulliverstravels
should be returned when I left the country, or paid for at the rate which | gulliverstravels
I would set upon them.”  I took up the two officers in my hands, put them | gulliverstravels
first into my coat-pockets, and then into every other pocket about me, | gulliverstravels
except my two fobs, and another secret pocket, which I had no mind should | gulliverstravels
be searched, wherein I had some little necessaries that were of no | gulliverstravels
consequence to any but myself.  In one of my fobs there was a silver | gulliverstravels
watch, and in the other a small quantity of gold in a purse.  These | gulliverstravels
gentlemen, having pen, ink, and paper, about them, made an exact | gulliverstravels
inventory of every thing they saw; and when they had done, desired I | gulliverstravels
would set them down, that they might deliver it to the emperor.  This | gulliverstravels
inventory I afterwards translated into English, and is, word for word, as | gulliverstravels
follows: | gulliverstravels
    “_Imprimis_: In the right coat-pocket of the great man-mountain” (for | gulliverstravels
    so I interpret the words _quinbus flestrin_,) “after the strictest | gulliverstravels
    search, we found only one great piece of coarse-cloth, large enough | gulliverstravels
    to be a foot-cloth for your majesty’s chief room of state.  In the | gulliverstravels
    left pocket we saw a huge silver chest, with a cover of the same | gulliverstravels
    metal, which we, the searchers, were not able to lift.  We desired it | gulliverstravels
    should be opened, and one of us stepping into it, found himself up to | gulliverstravels
    the mid leg in a sort of dust, some part whereof flying up to our | gulliverstravels
    faces set us both a sneezing for several times together.  In his | gulliverstravels
    right waistcoat-pocket we found a prodigious bundle of white thin | gulliverstravels
    substances, folded one over another, about the bigness of three men, | gulliverstravels
    tied with a strong cable, and marked with black figures; which we | gulliverstravels
    humbly conceive to be writings, every letter almost half as large as | gulliverstravels
    the palm of our hands.  In the left there was a sort of engine, from | gulliverstravels
    the back of which were extended twenty long poles, resembling the | gulliverstravels
    pallisados before your majesty’s court: wherewith we conjecture the | gulliverstravels
    man-mountain combs his head; for we did not always trouble him with | gulliverstravels
    questions, because we found it a great difficulty to make him | gulliverstravels
    understand us.  In the large pocket, on the right side of his middle | gulliverstravels
    cover” (so I translate the word _ranfulo_, by which they meant my | gulliverstravels
    breeches,) “we saw a hollow pillar of iron, about the length of a | gulliverstravels
    man, fastened to a strong piece of timber larger than the pillar; and | gulliverstravels
    upon one side of the pillar, were huge pieces of iron sticking out, | gulliverstravels
    cut into strange figures, which we know not what to make of.  In the | gulliverstravels
    left pocket, another engine of the same kind.  In the smaller pocket | gulliverstravels
    on the right side, were several round flat pieces of white and red | gulliverstravels
    metal, of different bulk; some of the white, which seemed to be | gulliverstravels
    silver, were so large and heavy, that my comrade and I could hardly | gulliverstravels
    lift them.  In the left pocket were two black pillars irregularly | gulliverstravels
    shaped: we could not, without difficulty, reach the top of them, as | gulliverstravels
    we stood at the bottom of his pocket.  One of them was covered, and | gulliverstravels
    seemed all of a piece: but at the upper end of the other there | gulliverstravels
    appeared a white round substance, about twice the bigness of our | gulliverstravels
    heads.  Within each of these was enclosed a prodigious plate of | gulliverstravels
    steel; which, by our orders, we obliged him to show us, because we | gulliverstravels
    apprehended they might be dangerous engines.  He took them out of | gulliverstravels
    their cases, and told us, that in his own country his practice was to | gulliverstravels
    shave his beard with one of these, and cut his meat with the other. | gulliverstravels
    There were two pockets which we could not enter: these he called his | gulliverstravels
    fobs; they were two large slits cut into the top of his middle cover, | gulliverstravels
    but squeezed close by the pressure of his belly.  Out of the right | gulliverstravels
    fob hung a great silver chain, with a wonderful kind of engine at the | gulliverstravels
    bottom.  We directed him to draw out whatever was at the end of that | gulliverstravels
    chain; which appeared to be a globe, half silver, and half of some | gulliverstravels
    transparent metal; for, on the transparent side, we saw certain | gulliverstravels
    strange figures circularly drawn, and thought we could touch them, | gulliverstravels
    till we found our fingers stopped by the lucid substance.  He put | gulliverstravels
    this engine into our ears, which made an incessant noise, like that | gulliverstravels
    of a water-mill: and we conjecture it is either some unknown animal, | gulliverstravels
    or the god that he worships; but we are more inclined to the latter | gulliverstravels
    opinion, because he assured us, (if we understood him right, for he | gulliverstravels
    expressed himself very imperfectly) that he seldom did any thing | gulliverstravels
    without consulting it.  He called it his oracle, and said, it pointed | gulliverstravels
    out the time for every action of his life.  From the left fob he took | gulliverstravels
    out a net almost large enough for a fisherman, but contrived to open | gulliverstravels
    and shut like a purse, and served him for the same use: we found | gulliverstravels
    therein several massy pieces of yellow metal, which, if they be real | gulliverstravels
    gold, must be of immense value. | gulliverstravels
    “Having thus, in obedience to your majesty’s commands, diligently | gulliverstravels
    searched all his pockets, we observed a girdle about his waist made | gulliverstravels
    of the hide of some prodigious animal, from which, on the left side, | gulliverstravels
    hung a sword of the length of five men; and on the right, a bag or | gulliverstravels
    pouch divided into two cells, each cell capable of holding three of | gulliverstravels
    your majesty’s subjects.  In one of these cells were several globes, | gulliverstravels
    or balls, of a most ponderous metal, about the bigness of our heads, | gulliverstravels
    and requiring a strong hand to lift them: the other cell contained a | gulliverstravels
    heap of certain black grains, but of no great bulk or weight, for we | gulliverstravels
    could hold above fifty of them in the palms of our hands. | gulliverstravels
    “This is an exact inventory of what we found about the body of the | gulliverstravels
    man-mountain, who used us with great civility, and due respect to | gulliverstravels
    your majesty’s commission.  Signed and sealed on the fourth day of | gulliverstravels
    the eighty-ninth moon of your majesty’s auspicious reign. | gulliverstravels
                                          CLEFRIN FRELOCK, MARSI FRELOCK.” | gulliverstravels
When this inventory was read over to the emperor, he directed me, | gulliverstravels
although in very gentle terms, to deliver up the several particulars.  He | gulliverstravels
first called for my scimitar, which I took out, scabbard and all.  In the | gulliverstravels
mean time he ordered three thousand of his choicest troops (who then | gulliverstravels
attended him) to surround me at a distance, with their bows and arrows | gulliverstravels
just ready to discharge; but I did not observe it, for mine eyes were | gulliverstravels
wholly fixed upon his majesty.  He then desired me to draw my scimitar, | gulliverstravels
which, although it had got some rust by the sea water, was, in most | gulliverstravels
parts, exceeding bright.  I did so, and immediately all the troops gave a | gulliverstravels
shout between terror and surprise; for the sun shone clear, and the | gulliverstravels
reflection dazzled their eyes, as I waved the scimitar to and fro in my | gulliverstravels
hand.  His majesty, who is a most magnanimous prince, was less daunted | gulliverstravels
than I could expect: he ordered me to return it into the scabbard, and | gulliverstravels
cast it on the ground as gently as I could, about six feet from the end | gulliverstravels
of my chain.  The next thing he demanded was one of the hollow iron | gulliverstravels
pillars; by which he meant my pocket pistols.  I drew it out, and at his | gulliverstravels
desire, as well as I could, expressed to him the use of it; and charging | gulliverstravels
it only with powder, which, by the closeness of my pouch, happened to | gulliverstravels
escape wetting in the sea (an inconvenience against which all prudent | gulliverstravels
mariners take special care to provide,) I first cautioned the emperor not | gulliverstravels
to be afraid, and then I let it off in the air.  The astonishment here | gulliverstravels
was much greater than at the sight of my scimitar.  Hundreds fell down as | gulliverstravels
if they had been struck dead; and even the emperor, although he stood his | gulliverstravels
ground, could not recover himself for some time.  I delivered up both my | gulliverstravels
pistols in the same manner as I had done my scimitar, and then my pouch | gulliverstravels
of powder and bullets; begging him that the former might be kept from | gulliverstravels
fire, for it would kindle with the smallest spark, and blow up his | gulliverstravels
imperial palace into the air.  I likewise delivered up my watch, which | gulliverstravels
the emperor was very curious to see, and commanded two of his tallest | gulliverstravels
yeomen of the guards to bear it on a pole upon their shoulders, as | gulliverstravels
draymen in England do a barrel of ale.  He was amazed at the continual | gulliverstravels
noise it made, and the motion of the minute-hand, which he could easily | gulliverstravels
discern; for their sight is much more acute than ours: he asked the | gulliverstravels
opinions of his learned men about it, which were various and remote, as | gulliverstravels
the reader may well imagine without my repeating; although indeed I could | gulliverstravels
not very perfectly understand them.  I then gave up my silver and copper | gulliverstravels
money, my purse, with nine large pieces of gold, and some smaller ones; | gulliverstravels
my knife and razor, my comb and silver snuff-box, my handkerchief and | gulliverstravels
journal-book.  My scimitar, pistols, and pouch, were conveyed in | gulliverstravels
carriages to his majesty’s stores; but the rest of my goods were returned | gulliverstravels
me. | gulliverstravels
I had as I before observed, one private pocket, which escaped their | gulliverstravels
search, wherein there was a pair of spectacles (which I sometimes use for | gulliverstravels
the weakness of mine eyes,) a pocket perspective, and some other little | gulliverstravels
conveniences; which, being of no consequence to the emperor, I did not | gulliverstravels
think myself bound in honour to discover, and I apprehended they might be | gulliverstravels
lost or spoiled if I ventured them out of my possession. | gulliverstravels
CHAPTER III. | gulliverstravels
The author diverts the emperor, and his nobility of both sexes, in a very | gulliverstravels
uncommon manner.  The diversions of the court of Lilliput described.  The | gulliverstravels
author has his liberty granted him upon certain conditions. | gulliverstravels
My gentleness and good behaviour had gained so far on the emperor and his | gulliverstravels
court, and indeed upon the army and people in general, that I began to | gulliverstravels
conceive hopes of getting my liberty in a short time.  I took all | gulliverstravels
possible methods to cultivate this favourable disposition.  The natives | gulliverstravels
came, by degrees, to be less apprehensive of any danger from me.  I would | gulliverstravels
sometimes lie down, and let five or six of them dance on my hand; and at | gulliverstravels
last the boys and girls would venture to come and play at hide-and-seek | gulliverstravels
in my hair.  I had now made a good progress in understanding and speaking | gulliverstravels
the language.  The emperor had a mind one day to entertain me with | gulliverstravels
several of the country shows, wherein they exceed all nations I have | gulliverstravels
known, both for dexterity and magnificence.  I was diverted with none so | gulliverstravels
much as that of the rope-dancers, performed upon a slender white thread, | gulliverstravels
extended about two feet, and twelve inches from the ground.  Upon which I | gulliverstravels
shall desire liberty, with the reader’s patience, to enlarge a little. | gulliverstravels
This diversion is only practised by those persons who are candidates for | gulliverstravels
great employments, and high favour at court.  They are trained in this | gulliverstravels
art from their youth, and are not always of noble birth, or liberal | gulliverstravels
education.  When a great office is vacant, either by death or disgrace | gulliverstravels
(which often happens,) five or six of those candidates petition the | gulliverstravels
emperor to entertain his majesty and the court with a dance on the rope; | gulliverstravels
and whoever jumps the highest, without falling, succeeds in the office. | gulliverstravels
Very often the chief ministers themselves are commanded to show their | gulliverstravels
skill, and to convince the emperor that they have not lost their faculty. | gulliverstravels
Flimnap, the treasurer, is allowed to cut a caper on the straight rope, | gulliverstravels
at least an inch higher than any other lord in the whole empire.  I have | gulliverstravels
seen him do the summerset several times together, upon a trencher fixed | gulliverstravels
on a rope which is no thicker than a common packthread in England.  My | gulliverstravels
friend Reldresal, principal secretary for private affairs, is, in my | gulliverstravels
opinion, if I am not partial, the second after the treasurer; the rest of | gulliverstravels
the great officers are much upon a par. | gulliverstravels
These diversions are often attended with fatal accidents, whereof great | gulliverstravels
numbers are on record.  I myself have seen two or three candidates break | gulliverstravels
a limb.  But the danger is much greater, when the ministers themselves | gulliverstravels
are commanded to show their dexterity; for, by contending to excel | gulliverstravels
themselves and their fellows, they strain so far that there is hardly one | gulliverstravels
of them who has not received a fall, and some of them two or three.  I | gulliverstravels
was assured that, a year or two before my arrival, Flimnap would | gulliverstravels
infallibly have broke his neck, if one of the king’s cushions, that | gulliverstravels
accidentally lay on the ground, had not weakened the force of his fall. | gulliverstravels
There is likewise another diversion, which is only shown before the | gulliverstravels
emperor and empress, and first minister, upon particular occasions.  The | gulliverstravels
emperor lays on the table three fine silken threads of six inches long; | gulliverstravels
one is blue, the other red, and the third green.  These threads are | gulliverstravels
proposed as prizes for those persons whom the emperor has a mind to | gulliverstravels
distinguish by a peculiar mark of his favour.  The ceremony is performed | gulliverstravels
in his majesty’s great chamber of state, where the candidates are to | gulliverstravels
undergo a trial of dexterity very different from the former, and such as | gulliverstravels
I have not observed the least resemblance of in any other country of the | gulliverstravels
new or old world.  The emperor holds a stick in his hands, both ends | gulliverstravels
parallel to the horizon, while the candidates advancing, one by one, | gulliverstravels
sometimes leap over the stick, sometimes creep under it, backward and | gulliverstravels
forward, several times, according as the stick is advanced or depressed. | gulliverstravels
Sometimes the emperor holds one end of the stick, and his first minister | gulliverstravels
the other; sometimes the minister has it entirely to himself.  Whoever | gulliverstravels
performs his part with most agility, and holds out the longest in leaping | gulliverstravels
and creeping, is rewarded with the blue-coloured silk; the red is given | gulliverstravels
to the next, and the green to the third, which they all wear girt twice | gulliverstravels
round about the middle; and you see few great persons about this court | gulliverstravels
who are not adorned with one of these girdles. | gulliverstravels
The horses of the army, and those of the royal stables, having been daily | gulliverstravels
led before me, were no longer shy, but would come up to my very feet | gulliverstravels
without starting.  The riders would leap them over my hand, as I held it | gulliverstravels
on the ground; and one of the emperor’s huntsmen, upon a large courser, | gulliverstravels
took my foot, shoe and all; which was indeed a prodigious leap.  I had | gulliverstravels
the good fortune to divert the emperor one day after a very extraordinary | gulliverstravels
manner.  I desired he would order several sticks of two feet high, and | gulliverstravels
the thickness of an ordinary cane, to be brought me; whereupon his | gulliverstravels
majesty commanded the master of his woods to give directions accordingly; | gulliverstravels
and the next morning six woodmen arrived with as many carriages, drawn by | gulliverstravels
eight horses to each.  I took nine of these sticks, and fixing them | gulliverstravels
firmly in the ground in a quadrangular figure, two feet and a half | gulliverstravels
square, I took four other sticks, and tied them parallel at each corner, | gulliverstravels
about two feet from the ground; then I fastened my handkerchief to the | gulliverstravels
nine sticks that stood erect; and extended it on all sides, till it was | gulliverstravels
tight as the top of a drum; and the four parallel sticks, rising about | gulliverstravels
five inches higher than the handkerchief, served as ledges on each side. | gulliverstravels
When I had finished my work, I desired the emperor to let a troop of his | gulliverstravels
best horses twenty-four in number, come and exercise upon this plain. | gulliverstravels
His majesty approved of the proposal, and I took them up, one by one, in | gulliverstravels
my hands, ready mounted and armed, with the proper officers to exercise | gulliverstravels
them.  As soon as they got into order they divided into two parties, | gulliverstravels
performed mock skirmishes, discharged blunt arrows, drew their swords, | gulliverstravels
fled and pursued, attacked and retired, and in short discovered the best | gulliverstravels
military discipline I ever beheld.  The parallel sticks secured them and | gulliverstravels
their horses from falling over the stage; and the emperor was so much | gulliverstravels
delighted, that he ordered this entertainment to be repeated several | gulliverstravels
days, and once was pleased to be lifted up and give the word of command; | gulliverstravels
and with great difficulty persuaded even the empress herself to let me | gulliverstravels
hold her in her close chair within two yards of the stage, when she was | gulliverstravels
able to take a full view of the whole performance.  It was my good | gulliverstravels
fortune, that no ill accident happened in these entertainments; only once | gulliverstravels
a fiery horse, that belonged to one of the captains, pawing with his | gulliverstravels
hoof, struck a hole in my handkerchief, and his foot slipping, he | gulliverstravels
overthrew his rider and himself; but I immediately relieved them both, | gulliverstravels
and covering the hole with one hand, I set down the troop with the other, | gulliverstravels
in the same manner as I took them up. The horse that fell was strained in | gulliverstravels
the left shoulder, but the rider got no hurt; and I repaired my | gulliverstravels
handkerchief as well as I could: however, I would not trust to the | gulliverstravels
strength of it any more, in such dangerous enterprises. | gulliverstravels
About two or three days before I was set at liberty, as I was | gulliverstravels
entertaining the court with this kind of feat, there arrived an express | gulliverstravels
to inform his majesty, that some of his subjects, riding near the place | gulliverstravels
where I was first taken up, had seen a great black substance lying on the | gulliverstravels
around, very oddly shaped, extending its edges round, as wide as his | gulliverstravels
majesty’s bedchamber, and rising up in the middle as high as a man; that | gulliverstravels
it was no living creature, as they at first apprehended, for it lay on | gulliverstravels
the grass without motion; and some of them had walked round it several | gulliverstravels
times; that, by mounting upon each other’s shoulders, they had got to the | gulliverstravels
top, which was flat and even, and, stamping upon it, they found that it | gulliverstravels
was hollow within; that they humbly conceived it might be something | gulliverstravels
belonging to the man-mountain; and if his majesty pleased, they would | gulliverstravels
undertake to bring it with only five horses.  I presently knew what they | gulliverstravels
meant, and was glad at heart to receive this intelligence.  It seems, | gulliverstravels
upon my first reaching the shore after our shipwreck, I was in such | gulliverstravels
confusion, that before I came to the place where I went to sleep, my hat, | gulliverstravels
which I had fastened with a string to my head while I was rowing, and had | gulliverstravels
stuck on all the time I was swimming, fell off after I came to land; the | gulliverstravels
string, as I conjecture, breaking by some accident, which I never | gulliverstravels
observed, but thought my hat had been lost at sea.  I entreated his | gulliverstravels
imperial majesty to give orders it might be brought to me as soon as | gulliverstravels
possible, describing to him the use and the nature of it: and the next | gulliverstravels
day the waggoners arrived with it, but not in a very good condition; they | gulliverstravels
had bored two holes in the brim, within an inch and half of the edge, and | gulliverstravels
fastened two hooks in the holes; these hooks were tied by a long cord to | gulliverstravels
the harness, and thus my hat was dragged along for above half an English | gulliverstravels
mile; but, the ground in that country being extremely smooth and level, | gulliverstravels
it received less damage than I expected. | gulliverstravels
Two days after this adventure, the emperor, having ordered that part of | gulliverstravels
his army which quarters in and about his metropolis, to be in readiness, | gulliverstravels
took a fancy of diverting himself in a very singular manner.  He desired | gulliverstravels
I would stand like a Colossus, with my legs as far asunder as I | gulliverstravels
conveniently could.  He then commanded his general (who was an old | gulliverstravels
experienced leader, and a great patron of mine) to draw up the troops in | gulliverstravels
close order, and march them under me; the foot by twenty-four abreast, | gulliverstravels
and the horse by sixteen, with drums beating, colours flying, and pikes | gulliverstravels
advanced.  This body consisted of three thousand foot, and a thousand | gulliverstravels
horse.  His majesty gave orders, upon pain of death, that every soldier | gulliverstravels
in his march should observe the strictest decency with regard to my | gulliverstravels
person; which however could not prevent some of the younger officers from | gulliverstravels
