turning up their eyes as they passed under me: and, to confess the truth, | gulliverstravels
my breeches were at that time in so ill a condition, that they afforded | gulliverstravels
some opportunities for laughter and admiration. | gulliverstravels
I had sent so many memorials and petitions for my liberty, that his | gulliverstravels
majesty at length mentioned the matter, first in the cabinet, and then in | gulliverstravels
a full council; where it was opposed by none, except Skyresh Bolgolam, | gulliverstravels
who was pleased, without any provocation, to be my mortal enemy.  But it | gulliverstravels
was carried against him by the whole board, and confirmed by the emperor. | gulliverstravels
That minister was _galbet_, or admiral of the realm, very much in his | gulliverstravels
master’s confidence, and a person well versed in affairs, but of a morose | gulliverstravels
and sour complexion.  However, he was at length persuaded to comply; but | gulliverstravels
prevailed that the articles and conditions upon which I should be set | gulliverstravels
free, and to which I must swear, should be drawn up by himself.  These | gulliverstravels
articles were brought to me by Skyresh Bolgolam in person attended by two | gulliverstravels
under-secretaries, and several persons of distinction.  After they were | gulliverstravels

their laws; which was, to hold my right foot in my left hand, and to | gulliverstravels
place the middle finger of my right hand on the crown of my head, and my | gulliverstravels
thumb on the tip of my right ear.  But because the reader may be curious | gulliverstravels

people, as well as to know the article upon which I recovered my liberty, | gulliverstravels
I have made a translation of the whole instrument, word for word, as near | gulliverstravels

“Golbasto Momarem Evlame Gurdilo Shefin Mully Ully Gue, most mighty | gulliverstravels
Emperor of Lilliput, delight and terror of the universe, whose dominions | gulliverstravels
extend five thousand _blustrugs_ (about twelve miles in circumference) to | gulliverstravels
the extremities of the globe; monarch of all monarchs, taller than the | gulliverstravels
sons of men; whose feet press down to the centre, and whose head strikes | gulliverstravels
against the sun; at whose nod the princes of the earth shake their knees; | gulliverstravels
pleasant as the spring, comfortable as the summer, fruitful as autumn, | gulliverstravels
dreadful as winter: his most sublime majesty proposes to the | gulliverstravels
man-mountain, lately arrived at our celestial dominions, the following | gulliverstravels
articles, which, by a solemn oath, he shall be obliged to perform:— | gulliverstravels
“1st, The man-mountain shall not depart from our dominions, without our | gulliverstravels
license under our great seal. | gulliverstravels
“2d, He shall not presume to come into our metropolis, without our | gulliverstravels
express order; at which time, the inhabitants shall have two hours | gulliverstravels
warning to keep within doors. | gulliverstravels
“3d, The said man-mountain shall confine his walks to our principal high | gulliverstravels
roads, and not offer to walk, or lie down, in a meadow or field of corn. | gulliverstravels
“4th, As he walks the said roads, he shall take the utmost care not to | gulliverstravels
trample upon the bodies of any of our loving subjects, their horses, or | gulliverstravels
carriages, nor take any of our subjects into his hands without their own | gulliverstravels
consent. | gulliverstravels
“5th, If an express requires extraordinary despatch, the man-mountain | gulliverstravels
shall be obliged to carry, in his pocket, the messenger and horse a six | gulliverstravels
days journey, once in every moon, and return the said messenger back (if | gulliverstravels
so required) safe to our imperial presence. | gulliverstravels
“6th, He shall be our ally against our enemies in the island of Blefuscu, | gulliverstravels
and do his utmost to destroy their fleet, which is now preparing to | gulliverstravels
invade us. | gulliverstravels
“7th, That the said man-mountain shall, at his times of leisure, be | gulliverstravels
aiding and assisting to our workmen, in helping to raise certain great | gulliverstravels
stones, towards covering the wall of the principal park, and other our | gulliverstravels
royal buildings. | gulliverstravels
“8th, That the said man-mountain shall, in two moons’ time, deliver in an | gulliverstravels
exact survey of the circumference of our dominions, by a computation of | gulliverstravels
his own paces round the coast. | gulliverstravels
“Lastly, That, upon his solemn oath to observe all the above articles, | gulliverstravels
the said man-mountain shall have a daily allowance of meat and drink | gulliverstravels
sufficient for the support of 1724 of our subjects, with free access to | gulliverstravels
our royal person, and other marks of our favour.  Given at our palace at | gulliverstravels
Belfaborac, the twelfth day of the ninety-first moon of our reign.” | gulliverstravels
I swore and subscribed to these articles with great cheerfulness and | gulliverstravels
content, although some of them were not so honourable as I could have | gulliverstravels
wished; which proceeded wholly from the malice of Skyresh Bolgolam, the | gulliverstravels
high-admiral: whereupon my chains were immediately unlocked, and I was at | gulliverstravels
full liberty.  The emperor himself, in person, did me the honour to be by | gulliverstravels
at the whole ceremony.  I made my acknowledgements by prostrating myself | gulliverstravels
at his majesty’s feet: but he commanded me to rise; and after many | gulliverstravels
gracious expressions, which, to avoid the censure of vanity, I shall not | gulliverstravels
repeat, he added, “that he hoped I should prove a useful servant, and | gulliverstravels
well deserve all the favours he had already conferred upon me, or might | gulliverstravels
do for the future.” | gulliverstravels
The reader may please to observe, that, in the last article of the | gulliverstravels
recovery of my liberty, the emperor stipulates to allow me a quantity of | gulliverstravels

﻿PRIDE AND PREJUDICE | prideandprejudice
By Jane Austen | prideandprejudice
Chapter 1 | prideandprejudice
It is a truth universally acknowledged, that a single man in possession | prideandprejudice
of a good fortune, must be in want of a wife. | prideandprejudice
However little known the feelings or views of such a man may be on his | prideandprejudice
first entering a neighbourhood, this truth is so well fixed in the minds | prideandprejudice
of the surrounding families, that he is considered the rightful property | prideandprejudice
of some one or other of their daughters. | prideandprejudice

Netherfield Park is let at last?” | prideandprejudice
Mr. Bennet replied that he had not. | prideandprejudice

told me all about it.” | prideandprejudice
Mr. Bennet made no answer. | prideandprejudice

“_You_ want to tell me, and I have no objection to hearing it.” | prideandprejudice
This was invitation enough. | prideandprejudice

Chapter 7 | prideandprejudice
Mr. Bennet's property consisted almost entirely in an estate of two | prideandprejudice
thousand a year, which, unfortunately for his daughters, was entailed, | prideandprejudice
